Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of the Opening Invocation in Hanafi Usul Works
Opening blessings of a Hanafi usul commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of the opening blessings (hamd and salawat) in a Hanafi usul text and explain why they precede legal discussions.

Core Idea
Hamd and salawat establish the theological foundation before engaging with legal theory.

Before any legal reasoning begins, classical Hanafi usul works open with praise of Allah and blessings on the Prophet. This is not mere formality; it frames the entire discipline within a theology of reliance on divine guidance. The opening passage you see here is the author's way of acknowledging that all knowledge and legal derivation flow from Allah and His Messenger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the opening
Locate the basmalah, the hamd (praise), and the salawat (blessings) in the Arabic text. Note how they are structured: beginning with divine names, then praise, then blessings on the Prophet and his companions.
This tripartite structure is standard in Islamic scholarly works.
2
Understand the theological implication
Recognize that the author attributes all authority to Allah 'the one who sent down verses and clear proofs'. This establishes that the sources of law (Quran and Sunnah) are divinely ordained.
The phrase 'You alone are sought for help' underscores reliance on Allah in deriving rulings.
3
Connect to usul al-fiqh methodology
Reflect on how this opening sets the scene: the commentator is about to explain a matn on usul, but first affirms that the ultimate source of legal knowledge is revelation. This frames all subsequent qiyas and istihsan as within the bounds of divine guidance.
The mention of 'four foundations' (al-arba'ah al-usul) hints at the Hanafi emphasis on the four sources.

The text of Muslim: "All praise is due to Allah who sent down the verses and sent the clear proofs, so the religion became manifest and certainty was impressed. Our Lord, to You belongs truth truly, and every metaphor is Yours; to You belongs command truly, and every metaphor is Yours. The reins of beginnings are in Your hand and the goals of ends are entrusted to You. You are the one sought for help and upon You is reliance. And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, who completed the judgments with the middlemost path, and was sent with comprehensive speech to the understandings of nations, and upon his family and companions who are the proofs of intellects, especially the four foundations." Translation: (Urdu paraphrase) Starting with the name of Allah...
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary. The author begins by quoting the matn of Muslim al-Thubut, which starts with the basmalah and hamd. The Arabic text praises Allah and sends blessings on the Prophet. The Urdu translation follows. This is a standard opening for a work of usul al-fiqh, establishing the theological foundation before delving into legal theory.

Key Terms
الحمد (al-hamd): Praise and thanks directed exclusively to Allah, acknowledging His attributes and blessings.
الصلاة والسلام (al-salat wa al-salam): Blessings and peace invoked upon the Prophet Muhammad, a customary act of reverence.
الاربعة الاصول (al-arba‘ah al-usul): The four foundations: referring to the first four Caliphs or the four sources of Islamic law (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) in context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the hamd passage in a Hanafi usul work?
A) To fulfill a requirement of scholarship before the Abbasid court
B) To affirm that all legal knowledge originates from Allah and His messenger
C) To demonstrate the author's proficiency in Arabic poetry
D) To provide a summary of the topics to be covered

Key Takeaway
The opening invocation in a Hanafi usul work is not decorative; it grounds the entire legal discipline in divine revelation and prophetic guidance.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Wisdom Behind Beginning with Al-Hamdu Lillah
Reasons for opening with hamdalah and the two modes of praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasons the author chose 'al-hamdu lillah' and distinguish between hamd salbi and hamd ijabi.

Core Idea
The author begins with 'al-hamdu lillah' to follow Quran, Sunnah, scholars, and acknowledge divine aid.

This lesson explores the author's deliberate choice of the opening phrase 'al-hamdu lillah'. We examine the multiple reasons he provides, from emulating the Quran and Sunnah to practicing both negative and positive praise of Allah, and why he used 'Subhanah' in another work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reasons
List the three reasons the author gives for beginning with 'al-hamdu lillah': following the Quran and Sunnah, emulating great scholars, and acknowledging divine assistance.
These reasons show the author's methodological commitment.
2
Understand the objection
The objection points out that the author began his other book with 'Subhanah'. Why the difference?
3
Distinguish praise types
Define hamd salbi (negative praise) and hamd ijabi (positive praise) and how 'Subhanah' and 'al-hamdu lillah' express them.
Hamd salbi: declaring Allah free from defects; hamd ijabi: affirming perfect attributes.
4
Appreciate the author's intent
The author covered both types of praise by using different openings, thereby practicing both methods of tahmid.
This reflects comprehensiveness in fulfilling the rights of praise.

قوله - الحمد - بعد تسمیہ تحمید ذکر کیا اس کی کئی وجہیں ہیں ۔
(الف) خیر الکلام کتاب اللہ کی اقتداء اور حدیث خیر الا نام رسول اللہ نے کی اتباع کرنا۔ (ب) اکابر علماء اعلام کی روش اور احبار امت کے مسلک کو اختیار کرنا۔
(ج) اس جلیلتہ الشان رفیعہ المرتبہ رسالہ کی تصنیف و تالیف چونکہ صرف اور صرف تائید ایزدی توفیق الہی اور اس کی خاص عنایت و غایت انعام کا ثمرہ ہے۔ اس لئے حتی الوسع اس کے بعض حقوق کی بجا آوری کے ارادہ سے کتاب کو الحمد اللہ سے شروع کیا۔
اعتراض : ۔ مصنف نے اپنی معرکۃ الآرا تصنیف "سلم العلوم میں حمد الہی بیان کرنے کے لئے خطبہ کو
"سبحانہ ما اعظم شانہ" سے شروع کیا اور اس کتاب مسلم میں الحمد اللہ سے کیوں شروع کیا ؟ جواب: - حمد الہی کی بجا آوری کا دوطریقہ ہے۔ ایک طریقہ حمد سلبی کا دوسر احمد ایجابی کا اللہ عز شانہ اور اس کے جملہ صفات کو تمام عیوب ونقائص اور شائبہ امکانات سے منزہ اور پاک ماننا اور زبان سے اس کی پاکی کا اقرار کرناحمد سلبی کہلاتا ہے ایسی حد کو "سبحانہ سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں چنانچہ قرآن حکیم میں کئی جگہ آیا ہے اور اللہ عز شانہ کے لئے تمام صفات کمالیہ مانا اور زبان سے اقرار کرنا حمد ایجابی کہلاتا ہے اس کا بھی ذکر قرآن مجید میں ہے جسکو الحمد اللہ سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں پس مصنف نے اپنی ایک کتاب کو حمد سلبی سے شروع کیا اور دوسری کتاب کو حمد ایجابی سے بیان کیا تا کہ تحمید کے دونوں طریقوں پر عمل ہو جائے۔
ایک معرکۃ الاختلاف : مقام تحمید میں علماء کے مابین ہمیشہ سے یہ اختلاف چلا آرہا ہے کہ جملہ الحمد اللہ منحوی اعتبار سے خبر یہ ہے یا انشائیہ، عبد القاھر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جملہ خبریہ ہے لیکن مراد لازم خبر یہ ہے اور وہ صفات کمال کا اظہار ہے اس لئے کہ اخبار کے لئے اظہار لازم ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف صاحب کشاف کا مختار یہ ہے کہ یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے جو جملہ خبریہ سے منقول ہے جیسا کہ بعت واشتریت باب عقود میں اور رحم الله و بارک اللہ وغیرہ باب دعاء میں اخبار سے انشاء کی طرف منقول ہے کہ ارحم اور بارک کے معنی میں ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی انشاء حمد کی طرف منقول ہے اور یہ راجح ہے کہ یہ مقام ، مقام انشاء حمد کا ہے نہ کہ اخبار کا۔ علماء کے اس اختلاف کو اجاگر کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے اپنے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔
"قالوا هذه الجملة يحتمل أن يكون انشائية لان المقام انشاء الجملة ويحتمل ان يكون خبرية لان الاخبار بالجملة يوجب الجملة انه اظهار صفات الكمال ، قيل لابد فى الجملة من ارادة ابتداء التعظيم وهذا ليس جزء ماهية الخبر بل معنى زائداً عليه المركب من المعنيين لاخارج له بل هو ابتداء معنى تلفظه عليه اقول لعل مرادهم الاخبار بهذا الخبر ملحوظاً فيه ارادة التعظيم يكون جملة اوح الخبر عند هم على حقيقته ولوسلم أن هذه الجملة جملة فالفرق أنها على تقدير كونها انشائية يكون منسلخة عن النسبة الخبرية كقولك رحمه الله بمعنى ارحمه وعلى تقدير كونها خبرية لايكون منسلخة عنها وان جعلت لمعنى خارج عن حقيقتها في لازم فائدة الخبر فتأمل"
حاشیہ کا خلاصہ :۔ یہ ہے کہ ”جملہ الحمد للہ کا مصنف کے نزدیک انشائیہ ہونا زیادہ راجح ہے اس لئے کہ یہ مقام انشاء حمد کا مقام ہے جبھی تو شق احتمال انشائیہ کو مقدم کیا اور انشائیہ ہونے کی دلیل کو خلل سے سالم قرار دیا۔ اس کے باوجود مصنف کے نزدیک اس جملہ کا خبر یہ ہونا بھی غلط نہیں اس لئے تمال خبر یہ کی شق کو مؤخر کیا اشارہ کرتے ہوئے کہ یہ جملہ خبریہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے چونکہ خبر یہ ہونا انشاء حمد کے منافی نہیں اس لئے کہ اخبار حمد ، انشاء حمد کو مستلزم ہے وہ اس طرح کہ اخبار حمد میں اس قول کا احداث و تکلم ضرور ہوتا ہے جو قول کہ اللہ عز شانہ تعالیٰ کے لئے تمام صفات کمالیہ مستجمعہ سے متصف ہونے پر بالا جمال دلالت کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ نسبت مدلولہ جو جملہ حد میں ملحوظ ہے وہ نسبت اس نسبت خارجیہ واقعیہ کے مطابق ہوتی ہے جو نسبت خارجیہ واقعیہ کہ اس جملہ خبریہ کے تلفظ کے لئے لازم ہے غرض الحمد اللہ کی نسبت خبریہ کے تکلم کے لئے اس کی نسبت واقعیہ کا لحاظ لازم ہے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ ملزوم کا تکلم و اخبار، لازم کے تکلم پر دال پر ہوتا ہے لہذا اخبار حمد کے وقت حمد واقعی کا اظہار ضرور ہے اور یہی انشاء ہے۔ عبارت حاشیہ کی تفصیلی توضیح - قوله في الحاشية قيل لابد في الجملة الخ ۔ اس عبارت میں جملہ حد کو جملہ خبریہ قرار دینے کی تعلیل مذکور پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔
اعتراض کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ جملہ خبریہ سے انشاء حمد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ انشاء حمد کے لئے محمود
His saying 'al-hamd' – after the basmala, he mentioned tahmid. There are several reasons for this: (a) Following the best speech, the Book of Allah, and following the hadith of the best of creation, the Messenger of Allah. (b) Adopting the way of the great scholars and the path of the narrators of the ummah. (c) Since the composition and authorship of this noble, high-ranking treatise is solely the result of divine support, divine success, and His special favor and utmost grace, therefore, to the extent of ability, with the intention of fulfilling some of its rights, he began the book with 'al-hamdu lillah'. Objection: The author began his renowned work 'Sullam al-'Ulum' with 'Subhanahu ma a'zama shanahu' for praising Allah, so why did he begin this book 'Muslim' with 'al-hamdu lillah'? Answer: There are two ways of praising Allah. One way is negative praise (hamd salbi) and the other is positive praise (hamd ijabi). Considering Allah and all His attributes free from all defects, imperfections, and traces of possibilities, and affirming His purity with the tongue, is called negative praise, expressed by 'Subhanah', as occurs in several places in the Quran. Affirming all attributes of perfection for Allah and affirming them with the tongue is called positive praise, also mentioned in the Quran, expressed by 'al-hamdu lillah'. Thus, the author began one of his books with negative praise and the other with positive praise so that both methods of tahmid are practiced. A point of contention: There has always been disagreement among scholars regarding the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' as to whether it is declarative or performative in terms of grammar. 'Abd al-Qahir's view is that it is declarative, but the intended meaning is the necessary implication of declaration, which is the expression of perfect attributes, because expression is necessary for declaration. In contrast, the author of al-Kashshaf's chosen view is that it is performative, transferred from declarative, just as in the chapter of contracts 'ba'tu' and 'ishtaraytu' and in the chapter of supplication 'rahimahu Allah' and 'baraka Allah' etc. are transferred from declaration to performance, meaning 'arhamhu' and 'barik'. Thus here too, it is transferred to performative praise, and the preferred view is that this station is a station of performative praise, not declaration. Highlighting this difference of scholars, the author said in his gloss: 'They said: This sentence could be performative because the station is the station of performing the sentence, and it could be declarative because declaring with the sentence entails the sentence being an expression of perfect attributes. It was said: In the sentence, intending the beginning of magnification is necessary, and this is not part of the essence of declaration but an additional meaning to it, composed of two meanings without loss; rather, it is the beginning of the meaning of its utterance. I say: Perhaps their intended meaning is that declaring with this information, with the intention of magnification being noted, makes the sentence... and the declaration in their view is in its reality. Even if we accept that this sentence is a sentence, the difference is that if it is considered performative, it is disconnected from the declarative relation, like your saying 'rahimahu Allah' meaning 'arhamhu'; and if it is considered declarative, it is not disconnected from it, even if it is made for a meaning outside its reality in the necessary benefit of declaration, so ponder.' Summary of the gloss: The author considers 'al-hamdu lillah' to be more likely performative because this is the station of performative praise, hence he gave precedence to the possibility of performative and deemed its evidence sound. Despite this, the author does not consider its being declarative as wrong, so he delayed the possibility of declarative, indicating that this sentence could also be declarative, because declarative does not contradict performative praise. Indeed, declaring praise entails performing praise. That is, in declaring praise, the utterance of this statement necessarily occurs, which indicates in summary that Allah is characterized by all perfect attributes. Because the relation of the meaning which is noted in the sentence 'al-hamd' corresponds to the external real relation which is necessary for the utterance of this declarative sentence. In short, for the utterance of the declarative relation of 'al-hamdu lillah', consideration of its real relation is necessary, and there is no doubt that the utterance and declaration of the necessary entails the utterance of the necessary. Therefore, at the time of declaring praise, the actual expression of praise is necessary, and that is the performance. Detailed explanation of the gloss: His saying in the gloss 'qila la budda fi al-jumlati al-kh' – In this phrase, an objection is made to the mentioned reasoning for considering the sentence 'al-hamd' as declarative. The formulation of the objection is that the declarative sentence cannot effect praise because for performative praise, the praised one...
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is from the front matter of the commentary. The author provides several reasons for beginning the book with 'al-hamdu lillah': following the Quran and Sunnah, emulating the great scholars, and acknowledging divine assistance. He then addresses an objection: why did he begin his other work 'Sullam al-'Ulum' with 'Subhanah'? He explains that there are two types of praise: negative (salbi) expressed by 'Subhanah' and positive (ijabi) expressed by 'al-hamdu lillah'. The author used both to practice both forms. Following this, the passage discusses a longstanding grammatical dispute among scholars: whether the sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' is declarative (khabariyya) or performative (insha'iyya). 'Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani held it is declarative, while the author of al-Kashshaf (Zamakhshari) held it is performative, transferred from declarative like contractual expressions. The author's own view, as expressed in his gloss, is that the performative interpretation is stronger because the context is one of performing praise. However, he does not reject the declarative possibility, since declaring praise necessarily entails performing it. The passage then delves into a detailed analysis of the gloss, explaining how even if the sentence is declarative, the act of declaring necessarily involves uttering the words, which itself constitutes the performance of praise. The text cuts off as it continues to elaborate on an objection against the view that a declarative sentence can effect praise.

Key Terms
الحمد لله (al-hamdu lillah): The phrase 'Praise be to Allah', used by the author to begin the book, expressing positive praise (hamd ijabi).
تحميد (tahmid): The act of praising Allah, specifically by saying 'al-hamdu lillah'.
حمد سلبي (hamd salbi): Negative praise: declaring Allah free from all defects, expressed by 'Subhanah'.
حمد إيجابي (hamd ijabi): Positive praise: affirming perfect attributes for Allah, expressed by 'al-hamdu lillah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the author began his book with 'al-hamdu lillah'?
A) Because it is the longest form of praise.
B) To practice positive praise, having used negative praise in another work.
C) Because he was forced by his teachers.
D) Because it is easier to pronounce.

Key Takeaway
The author begins with 'al-hamdu lillah' as a deliberate act to follow the Quran, Sunnah, and scholars, and to practice positive praise, complementing his use of negative praise in another work.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Grammatical Dispute: Declarative or Performative?
Grammatical dispute on the nature of 'al-hamdu lillah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the debate over whether 'al-hamdu lillah' is declarative or performative and state the author's preferred view.

Core Idea
The sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' is performative praise, not declarative, because the context demands performing praise.

This lesson delves into a long-standing grammatical debate: is the opening phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' a declarative statement or a performative act of praise? We examine the arguments of 'Abd al-Qahir and the author of al-Kashshaf, and the author's own analysis in his gloss, concluding that the performative interpretation is stronger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Know that 'Abd al-Qahir held it as declarative (khabariyya) while the author of al-Kashshaf (Zamakhshari) held it as performative (insha'iyya).
Declarative: reports a fact; performative: enacts the praise.
2
Understand the reasoning
For declarative: the sentence expresses perfect attributes, which is inherent to declaration. For performative: the context is one of performing praise, like contractual expressions.
3
Analyze the author's gloss
The author notes that performative is more likely because the station is performative, but declarative is not rejected since declaration entails performance.
The author gives precedence to performative while acknowledging declarative possibility.
4
Reconcile the two
Even if declarative, the act of uttering the declaration itself enacts praise, so both views lead to the same practical effect.
The difference is theoretical but impacts understanding of the nature of the sentence.

قوله - الحمد - بعد تسمیہ تحمید ذکر کیا اس کی کئی وجہیں ہیں ۔
(الف) خیر الکلام کتاب اللہ کی اقتداء اور حدیث خیر الا نام رسول اللہ نے کی اتباع کرنا۔ (ب) اکابر علماء اعلام کی روش اور احبار امت کے مسلک کو اختیار کرنا۔
(ج) اس جلیلتہ الشان رفیعہ المرتبہ رسالہ کی تصنیف و تالیف چونکہ صرف اور صرف تائید ایزدی توفیق الہی اور اس کی خاص عنایت و غایت انعام کا ثمرہ ہے۔ اس لئے حتی الوسع اس کے بعض حقوق کی بجا آوری کے ارادہ سے کتاب کو الحمد اللہ سے شروع کیا۔
اعتراض : ۔ مصنف نے اپنی معرکۃ الآرا تصنیف "سلم العلوم میں حمد الہی بیان کرنے کے لئے خطبہ کو
"سبحانہ ما اعظم شانہ" سے شروع کیا اور اس کتاب مسلم میں الحمد اللہ سے کیوں شروع کیا ؟ جواب: - حمد الہی کی بجا آوری کا دوطریقہ ہے۔ ایک طریقہ حمد سلبی کا دوسر احمد ایجابی کا اللہ عز شانہ اور اس کے جملہ صفات کو تمام عیوب ونقائص اور شائبہ امکانات سے منزہ اور پاک ماننا اور زبان سے اس کی پاکی کا اقرار کرناحمد سلبی کہلاتا ہے ایسی حد کو "سبحانہ سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں چنانچہ قرآن حکیم میں کئی جگہ آیا ہے اور اللہ عز شانہ کے لئے تمام صفات کمالیہ مانا اور زبان سے اقرار کرنا حمد ایجابی کہلاتا ہے اس کا بھی ذکر قرآن مجید میں ہے جسکو الحمد اللہ سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں پس مصنف نے اپنی ایک کتاب کو حمد سلبی سے شروع کیا اور دوسری کتاب کو حمد ایجابی سے بیان کیا تا کہ تحمید کے دونوں طریقوں پر عمل ہو جائے۔
ایک معرکۃ الاختلاف : مقام تحمید میں علماء کے مابین ہمیشہ سے یہ اختلاف چلا آرہا ہے کہ جملہ الحمد اللہ منحوی اعتبار سے خبر یہ ہے یا انشائیہ، عبد القاھر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جملہ خبریہ ہے لیکن مراد لازم خبر یہ ہے اور وہ صفات کمال کا اظہار ہے اس لئے کہ اخبار کے لئے اظہار لازم ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف صاحب کشاف کا مختار یہ ہے کہ یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے جو جملہ خبریہ سے منقول ہے جیسا کہ بعت واشتریت باب عقود میں اور رحم الله و بارک اللہ وغیرہ باب دعاء میں اخبار سے انشاء کی طرف منقول ہے کہ ارحم اور بارک کے معنی میں ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی انشاء حمد کی طرف منقول ہے اور یہ راجح ہے کہ یہ مقام ، مقام انشاء حمد کا ہے نہ کہ اخبار کا۔ علماء کے اس اختلاف کو اجاگر کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے اپنے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔
"قالوا هذه الجملة يحتمل أن يكون انشائية لان المقام انشاء الجملة ويحتمل ان يكون خبرية لان الاخبار بالجملة يوجب الجملة انه اظهار صفات الكمال ، قيل لابد فى الجملة من ارادة ابتداء التعظيم وهذا ليس جزء ماهية الخبر بل معنى زائداً عليه المركب من المعنيين لاخارج له بل هو ابتداء معنى تلفظه عليه اقول لعل مرادهم الاخبار بهذا الخبر ملحوظاً فيه ارادة التعظيم يكون جملة اوح الخبر عند هم على حقيقته ولوسلم أن هذه الجملة جملة فالفرق أنها على تقدير كونها انشائية يكون منسلخة عن النسبة الخبرية كقولك رحمه الله بمعنى ارحمه وعلى تقدير كونها خبرية لايكون منسلخة عنها وان جعلت لمعنى خارج عن حقيقتها في لازم فائدة الخبر فتأمل"
حاشیہ کا خلاصہ :۔ یہ ہے کہ ”جملہ الحمد للہ کا مصنف کے نزدیک انشائیہ ہونا زیادہ راجح ہے اس لئے کہ یہ مقام انشاء حمد کا مقام ہے جبھی تو شق احتمال انشائیہ کو مقدم کیا اور انشائیہ ہونے کی دلیل کو خلل سے سالم قرار دیا۔ اس کے باوجود مصنف کے نزدیک اس جملہ کا خبر یہ ہونا بھی غلط نہیں اس لئے تمال خبر یہ کی شق کو مؤخر کیا اشارہ کرتے ہوئے کہ یہ جملہ خبریہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے چونکہ خبر یہ ہونا انشاء حمد کے منافی نہیں اس لئے کہ اخبار حمد ، انشاء حمد کو مستلزم ہے وہ اس طرح کہ اخبار حمد میں اس قول کا احداث و تکلم ضرور ہوتا ہے جو قول کہ اللہ عز شانہ تعالیٰ کے لئے تمام صفات کمالیہ مستجمعہ سے متصف ہونے پر بالا جمال دلالت کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ نسبت مدلولہ جو جملہ حد میں ملحوظ ہے وہ نسبت اس نسبت خارجیہ واقعیہ کے مطابق ہوتی ہے جو نسبت خارجیہ واقعیہ کہ اس جملہ خبریہ کے تلفظ کے لئے لازم ہے غرض الحمد اللہ کی نسبت خبریہ کے تکلم کے لئے اس کی نسبت واقعیہ کا لحاظ لازم ہے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ ملزوم کا تکلم و اخبار، لازم کے تکلم پر دال پر ہوتا ہے لہذا اخبار حمد کے وقت حمد واقعی کا اظہار ضرور ہے اور یہی انشاء ہے۔ عبارت حاشیہ کی تفصیلی توضیح - قوله في الحاشية قيل لابد في الجملة الخ ۔ اس عبارت میں جملہ حد کو جملہ خبریہ قرار دینے کی تعلیل مذکور پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔
اعتراض کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ جملہ خبریہ سے انشاء حمد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ انشاء حمد کے لئے محمود
His saying 'al-hamd' – after the basmala, he mentioned tahmid. There are several reasons for this: (a) Following the best speech, the Book of Allah, and following the hadith of the best of creation, the Messenger of Allah. (b) Adopting the way of the great scholars and the path of the narrators of the ummah. (c) Since the composition and authorship of this noble, high-ranking treatise is solely the result of divine support, divine success, and His special favor and utmost grace, therefore, to the extent of ability, with the intention of fulfilling some of its rights, he began the book with 'al-hamdu lillah'. Objection: The author began his renowned work 'Sullam al-'Ulum' with 'Subhanahu ma a'zama shanahu' for praising Allah, so why did he begin this book 'Muslim' with 'al-hamdu lillah'? Answer: There are two ways of praising Allah. One way is negative praise (hamd salbi) and the other is positive praise (hamd ijabi). Considering Allah and all His attributes free from all defects, imperfections, and traces of possibilities, and affirming His purity with the tongue, is called negative praise, expressed by 'Subhanah', as occurs in several places in the Quran. Affirming all attributes of perfection for Allah and affirming them with the tongue is called positive praise, also mentioned in the Quran, expressed by 'al-hamdu lillah'. Thus, the author began one of his books with negative praise and the other with positive praise so that both methods of tahmid are practiced. A point of contention: There has always been disagreement among scholars regarding the phrase 'al-hamdu lillah' as to whether it is declarative or performative in terms of grammar. 'Abd al-Qahir's view is that it is declarative, but the intended meaning is the necessary implication of declaration, which is the expression of perfect attributes, because expression is necessary for declaration. In contrast, the author of al-Kashshaf's chosen view is that it is performative, transferred from declarative, just as in the chapter of contracts 'ba'tu' and 'ishtaraytu' and in the chapter of supplication 'rahimahu Allah' and 'baraka Allah' etc. are transferred from declaration to performance, meaning 'arhamhu' and 'barik'. Thus here too, it is transferred to performative praise, and the preferred view is that this station is a station of performative praise, not declaration. Highlighting this difference of scholars, the author said in his gloss: 'They said: This sentence could be performative because the station is the station of performing the sentence, and it could be declarative because declaring with the sentence entails the sentence being an expression of perfect attributes. It was said: In the sentence, intending the beginning of magnification is necessary, and this is not part of the essence of declaration but an additional meaning to it, composed of two meanings without loss; rather, it is the beginning of the meaning of its utterance. I say: Perhaps their intended meaning is that declaring with this information, with the intention of magnification being noted, makes the sentence... and the declaration in their view is in its reality. Even if we accept that this sentence is a sentence, the difference is that if it is considered performative, it is disconnected from the declarative relation, like your saying 'rahimahu Allah' meaning 'arhamhu'; and if it is considered declarative, it is not disconnected from it, even if it is made for a meaning outside its reality in the necessary benefit of declaration, so ponder.' Summary of the gloss: The author considers 'al-hamdu lillah' to be more likely performative because this is the station of performative praise, hence he gave precedence to the possibility of performative and deemed its evidence sound. Despite this, the author does not consider its being declarative as wrong, so he delayed the possibility of declarative, indicating that this sentence could also be declarative, because declarative does not contradict performative praise. Indeed, declaring praise entails performing praise. That is, in declaring praise, the utterance of this statement necessarily occurs, which indicates in summary that Allah is characterized by all perfect attributes. Because the relation of the meaning which is noted in the sentence 'al-hamd' corresponds to the external real relation which is necessary for the utterance of this declarative sentence. In short, for the utterance of the declarative relation of 'al-hamdu lillah', consideration of its real relation is necessary, and there is no doubt that the utterance and declaration of the necessary entails the utterance of the necessary. Therefore, at the time of declaring praise, the actual expression of praise is necessary, and that is the performance. Detailed explanation of the gloss: His saying in the gloss 'qila la budda fi al-jumlati al-kh' – In this phrase, an objection is made to the mentioned reasoning for considering the sentence 'al-hamd' as declarative. The formulation of the objection is that the declarative sentence cannot effect praise because for performative praise, the praised one...
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is from the front matter of the commentary. The author provides several reasons for beginning the book with 'al-hamdu lillah': following the Quran and Sunnah, emulating the great scholars, and acknowledging divine assistance. He then addresses an objection: why did he begin his other work 'Sullam al-'Ulum' with 'Subhanah'? He explains that there are two types of praise: negative (salbi) expressed by 'Subhanah' and positive (ijabi) expressed by 'al-hamdu lillah'. The author used both to practice both forms. Following this, the passage discusses a longstanding grammatical dispute among scholars: whether the sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' is declarative (khabariyya) or performative (insha'iyya). 'Abd al-Qahir al-Jurjani held it is declarative, while the author of al-Kashshaf (Zamakhshari) held it is performative, transferred from declarative like contractual expressions. The author's own view, as expressed in his gloss, is that the performative interpretation is stronger because the context is one of performing praise. However, he does not reject the declarative possibility, since declaring praise necessarily entails performing it. The passage then delves into a detailed analysis of the gloss, explaining how even if the sentence is declarative, the act of declaring necessarily involves uttering the words, which itself constitutes the performance of praise. The text cuts off as it continues to elaborate on an objection against the view that a declarative sentence can effect praise.

Key Terms
جملة خبرية (jumla khabariyya): A declarative sentence that can be true or false; here, some scholars consider 'al-hamdu lillah' as such.
جملة إنشائية (jumla insha'iyya): A performative sentence that enacts its content, like 'I praise' rather than 'I declare'; preferred by the author for 'al-hamdu lillah' in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author consider the performative interpretation of 'al-hamdu lillah' to be more likely?
A) Because the sentence is transferred from a declarative origin.
B) Because the context is one of performing praise.
C) Because 'Abd al-Qahir said it is declarative.
D) Because performative sentences are always preferred in openings.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical nature of 'al-hamdu lillah' is debated, but the author leans toward performative, reconciling it with declarative by showing that declaration enacts praise.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Reins of Beginnings: Allah's Control Over the Principles of Usul al-Fiqh
Commentary on the opening supplication's first two clauses and the statement of reliance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of 'mabadi' in the context of usul al-fiqh and describe how the opening supplication establishes tawhid as the foundation of the science.

Core Idea
All beginnings and principles, especially of usul al-fiqh, are under Allah's complete control.

The commentator unpacks the author's opening words: 'The reins of beginnings are in Your hand.' This is not just a poetic flourish; it is a profound statement about the nature of knowledge. The 'beginnings' (mabadi) refer to the foundational causes and principles of each science. By placing them in Allah's hand, the author grounds the entire study of usul al-fiqh in divine sovereignty. In this lesson, we will dissect the metaphor and understand its theological and methodological significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms: a'innah and mabadi
Recognize that a'innah (reins) symbolizes control and mabadi (beginnings) means foundational principles or causes.
The commentator notes that mabadi can refer to the principles of a science.
2
Understand the metaphor
The author likens the principles to mounts that carry a rider to the destination, but only mentions the reins. This is isti'arah bil-kinayah.
The commentator identifies two layers of metaphor.
3
Apply to usul al-fiqh
The commentator explicitly states that 'beginnings' here especially means the principles of usul al-fiqh.
This makes the supplication directly relevant to the study of usul.
4
Theological implication
The supplication alludes to the Quranic phrase 'fa''al lima yurid' (Doer of whatever He intends), affirming that all causation is from Allah.
This reinforces tawhid.
5
Reliance on Allah
The supplication leads to the statement of tawakkul: we rely only on Allah, not on the means themselves.
The statement 'For You are the One sought for help, and upon You is reliance' concludes the thought.

قوله - اعنة المبادی بیدیک - اعنہ عنان کی جمع ہے اردو میں لگام کو کہتے ہیں مبادی، مبدا کی جمع ہے ہرشی کے اول کو یا جس پر اشیاء کا وجود موقوف ہو یعنی موقوف علیہ کو مبادی کہتے ہیں اس سے مراد اسباب ہیں۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اوامر و اسباب سب اللہ تعالی کے ہی پیدا کرنے سے ہیں وہ جو چاہتا ہے کرتا ہے اور جو چاہتا ہے حکم دیتا ہے اس سے اشارہ ہے آیت کریمہ فعال لما یرید کی طرف۔ مبادی سے یہاں پر خاص مبادی علوم بھی مراد لئے جاسکتے ہیں، خصوصاً مبادی اصول فقہ مراد لینا زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ اور ہرفن کے مبادی چونکہ اس فن کے مسائل ہوتے ہیں پس اس وقت عبارت کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ ہر فن خصوصاً اصول فقہ کے مبادی یعنی اس کے مسائل وقواعد تیرے ہی قبضہ واختیار میں ہیں جس کسی کو جو حاصل ہو گا تیرے ہی عطا کرنے سے حاصل ہوگا۔
قوله ونواصى المقاصد مفوضة الیک : ۔ اس کا قول نواصی، ناصیہ کی جمع ہے موئے پیشانی کو کہتے ہیں یا ہر چہار طرف بال اگنے کی منتہاء کو کہتے ہیں۔ مقاصد ، مقصد کی جمع ہے مطلب کے معنی میں ہے۔ مفوضته ، تفویض کا اسم مفعول مؤنث ، ردالیہ یا مردودۃ کے معنی میں ہے۔ ان دونوں جملوں میں حضرت مصنف نے جن براعت ظاہرہ اور فصاحت و بلاغت کا جو ہر دکھلایا ہے تفطن پرمخفی نہیں ۔ يادر ہے کہ مصنف نے مبادی ( اسباب) کو ان مراکب سے تشبیہ دی ہے جو سواروں کو منزل مقصود تک لے جاتے ہیں مگر مراکب جو مشبہ يہ ہے کا ذکر نہیں کیا ہے صرف مشبہ جو مبادی ہے کا ذکر کیا ہے البتہ مشبہ بہ کے لوازم میں سے عنان کو ذکر کیا ہے فن میں اس طرز تحریر کو استعارہ بالکنایہ کہتے ہیں پھر مبادی کے لئے اعنہ کا اثبات استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے، اسی طرح اہم ترین مقصد مشکل فن اور لابنخل مسائل کو شریر اور بدکنے والے جانوروں سے تشبیہ دی جو بمشکل ہاتھ آتے ہیں جن کو ان کے پیشانی کے بال پکڑ کر قابو میں کیا جاتا ہے مگر مشبہ بہ کو ذکر نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اس کے لوازم میں سے نواصی کو ذکر کیا ہے یہ بھی استعارہ بالکنایہ ہے اور پھر مقاصد کے لئے نواصی کا اثبات استعارہ تخیليہ ہے۔
قوله فانت المستعان وعليك التكلان : فاء تفريعية ہے، مستعان استعانت سے اسم مفعول ہے وہ ذات جس سے مدد مانگی جائے اس کو مستعان کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا قول تكلان اسم ہے تو كل کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور توكل ، اظہار بجز اور غير پر اعتماد کرنے کو کہتے ہیں معنی يہ ہے کہ اے ہمارے پروردگار ! جب تو ایسا ہے کہ مطالب و مقاصد اور مبادی واسباب سب تیرے ہی قبضہ واختیار میں میں اس لئے ہم تجھی پر بھروسہ کرتے ہیں اور تجھی سے مدد طلب کرتے ہیں مبادی واسباب سے مدد نہیں طلب کرتے کہ وہ از قبیل شرائط وروابط میں جو غیر مستقل اور خود محتاج ہوتے ہیں پس تیرے غیر پر کیسے بھروسہ کر سکتے ہیں۔
قوله والصلوة والسلام على سيدنا محمد ع الله : ۔ اللہ عز شانہ کے بندوں پر اتنے انعامات واحسانات ہیں جن کا حساب و شمار ممکن نہیں ارشا در بانی ہے فان تعدوها فلا تحصوها ۔ پس اس لئے اس کی غیر متناہی نعمتوں کے شکرانے میں حمد النہی بیان کیا، پھر دنیا کی ان تمام نعمتوں میں سب سے عظیم ترین وافضل نعمت ایمان ہے کہ اس پر اخروی حیات جاودانی اور اسکی کامیابی کا مدار ہے اور یہ عظیم دولت مسلمانوں کو پیغمبر اسلام ھادی اعظم نور مجسم حضرت محمد لے کے واسطہ سے ملی ہے تو ضروری ہو گیا کہ حمد الہی کے بعد فورا شکر ھادی ادا کیا جائے جیسا کہ آپ نے کا ارشاد ہے من لم يشكر الناس لم يشكر الله اس لئے حضرت مصنف نے حمد کے بعد صلوۃ وسلام پیش کیا اور تا کہ آیت يايها الذين امنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسلیما پر بھی عمل ہو جائے پس کہا والصلوة والسلام الخ
قوله المتمم للحكم: تميم سے اسم فاعل کا صیغہ ہے اکمال کے معنی میں ہے اس میں تلويح ہے حديث پاک بعثت لاتم مكارم الاخلاق کی طرف۔ اس میں اسناد مجازی ہے حکم جمع ہے حکمت کی ۔موجودات کے احوال واقعیہ ، بقدر طاقت بشر يہ جاننے کو حکمت کہتے ہیں، حکمت کی دو قسمیں ہیں حکمت نظریہ، حکمت عملیہ ۔ اول سے عقائد و اصول مراد ہیں اور نانی سے اخلاق مرضیہ واعمال صالحہ مراد ہیں اس لئے کہ حکمت کا اطلاق عدل و علم، حلم، نبوت، فقہ قرآن شریعت سب پر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے من يوتى الحكمة فقد اوتى خيراً كثيراً ۔ عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ حصور تے کو اللہ عز شانہ نے حکمت کے جملہ انواع و اقسام کا جامع اور تم بنا کر مبعوث کیا ہے حالانکہ پیشر وانبیاء کرام علیہم السلام کو بھی حکمتیں عطا کی گئیں تھیں تاہم وہ نامکمل تھیں مگر حضور سید تا آخرالزماں جاتا ہے کو حکمت تامہ کاملہ بالغہ عطا کی گئی اس لئے آپ نے فرمایا بعثت لاتمم مكارم الاخلاق
His statement: 'The reins of beginnings are in Your hand' — a'innah is the plural of inan, which in Urdu means 'reins'. Mabadi is the plural of mabda', meaning the beginning of something or that upon which the existence of things depends, i.e., the prerequisite; what is meant here are causes. The meaning is that commands and causes all are from the creation of Allah Almighty; He does what He wills and commands what He wills. This alludes to the noble verse 'Doer of whatever He intends'. Here, by 'beginnings' the beginnings of sciences can also be specifically intended, and it is more apparent to intend specifically the beginnings of usul al-fiqh. And since the beginnings of every discipline are the issues of that discipline, then the meaning of the expression is that the beginnings of every discipline, especially usul al-fiqh, i.e., its issues and rules, are in Your grasp and control; whoever obtains anything obtains it only from Your bestowal.
His statement: 'And the forelocks of objectives are entrusted to You' — nawasi is the plural of nasiyah, meaning the hair of the forehead or the end of where hair grows on all four sides. Maqasid is the plural of maqsad, meaning ‘intent.’ Mufawwadah is a feminine passive participle of tafwid, meaning ‘returned’ or ‘referred.’ In these two sentences, the manifest excellence, eloquence and rhetoric that the author has shown is not hidden from the attentive. It should be remembered that the author likened 'beginnings' (causes) to mounts that carry riders to the intended destination, but he did not mention the 'mounts' — the thing being likened — rather he only mentioned the 'beginnings' — the thing being likened — and mentioned from among the requisites of the thing-to-which-likened the 'reins'; in the art this style is called isti'arah bil-kinayah. Then, affirming 'reins' for 'beginnings' is isti'arah takhyiliyyah. Similarly, he likened the most important objectives — the difficult art and tangled issues — to wild, kicking animals that are hardly caught, and are controlled by catching their forelocks, but he did not mention the thing-to-which-likened; rather he mentioned from among its requisites the 'forelocks' — this also is isti'arah bil-kinayah; and then affirming 'forelocks' for 'objectives' is isti'arah takhyiliyyah.
His statement: 'For You are the One sought for help, and upon You is reliance' — the fa' is for detailing; musta'an is a passive participle from isti'anah, meaning the entity from whom help is sought. His word tuklan is a noun used in the sense of tawakkul, and tawakkul means expressing dependence on other than oneself. The meaning is: O our Lord! Since You are such that all requests and objectives, beginnings and causes are all in Your grasp and control, therefore we rely only on You and seek help only from You; we do not seek help from beginnings and causes, because they are of the category of conditions and means which are non-independent and themselves in need — so how can we rely on other than You?
His statement: 'And peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad' — Allah Almighty has so many favors and blessings upon His servants that counting them is impossible; as He said: 'If you count them, you cannot enumerate them.' Therefore, in gratitude for His endless blessings, the author expressed praise of Allah. Then, among all the blessings of this world, the greatest and most virtuous blessing is faith, upon which eternal life in the hereafter and its success depend; and this great wealth came to Muslims through the Prophet of Islam, the greatest guide, the embodied light, our master Muhammad, so it became necessary that after the praise of Allah, gratitude to the guide be expressed immediately, as the Prophet said: 'Whoever does not thank people has not thanked Allah.' Therefore, the author presented salawat and salam after the praise, and also to act upon the verse 'O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with salutations of peace.' So he said 'And peace and blessings...' etc.
His statement: 'The completer of wisdom' — it is the form of the active participle from tatmim, meaning completion. There is an allusion in it to the noble hadith: 'I was sent to complete the noble character traits.' This is a metaphorical attribution. Hikam is plural of hikmah. Knowing the real states of existing things to the extent of human capacity is called hikmah. There are two types of hikmah: theoretical wisdom and practical wisdom. The first refers to beliefs and principles, and the second refers to pleasing character and righteous deeds, because hikmah is applied to justice, knowledge, forbearance, prophethood, jurisprudence, the Quran, and the shariah. Thus the saying: 'Whoever is given hikmah has been given abundant good.' The meaning of the phrase is that the Prophet was sent by Allah Almighty as one who encompasses all types and kinds of hikmah, while previous prophets were also granted wisdoms, but they were incomplete; however, our master, the Seal of the Prophets, was granted complete, perfect, and mature wisdom. Therefore he said: 'I was sent to complete noble character traits.'
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the opening lines of the matn. The author, a Hanafi scholar, explains the metaphorical language used by the original author. First, 'the reins of beginnings are in Your hand' — 'reins' symbolizing control, and 'beginnings' meaning causes or the foundational principles. This affirms that all causes and commands are from Allah alone, alluding to the Quranic phrase 'Doer of whatever He intends.' The commentator notes that 'beginnings' can specifically refer to the principles of each science, especially usul al-fiqh, so the phrase means that the rules and principles of the science are under God's control. Next, 'the forelocks of objectives are entrusted to You' — 'forelocks' symbolize control like reins, and 'objectives' are the difficult goals of the science. The author uses a double metaphor: first likening causes to mounts (not explicitly mentioned) and objectives to wild animals, then mentioning only the reins and forelocks. This is identified as isti'arah bil-kinayah (metaphor by implication) and isti'arah takhyiliyyah (imaginary metaphor). Then the phrase 'For You are the One sought for help, and upon You is reliance' — explains that since everything is in God's hands, we only rely on Him, not on intermediate means. Then 'And peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad' — the commentator explains the structure of the author's preface: after praising God (not included here) for countless blessings, he sends blessings on the Prophet because faith is the greatest blessing and it came through him. This also fulfills the Quranic command to send salawat. Finally, 'the completer of wisdom' — the Prophet is described as the one who perfected wisdom, alluding to the hadith 'I was sent to complete noble character.' Wisdom (hikmah) is defined broadly as knowledge of realities, including beliefs and ethics. The commentator concludes that previous prophets had partial wisdom, but the Prophet Muhammad had complete wisdom, perfecting what came before.

Key Terms
مبادی (mabadi): Beginnings; that upon which the existence of things depends; causes or principles of a science.
اعنة (a'innah): Plural of 'inan'; reins used to control a mount.
نواصی (nawasi): Plural of nasiyah; forelock or hair of the forehead.
مستعان (musta'aan): The one from whom help is sought; passive participle of isti'anah.
توكل (tawakkul): Expressing dependence on another; reliance.
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'arah bil-kinayah): A metaphor where the thing being likened is not mentioned, but only a requisite of the thing to which it is likened is mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'mabadi' primarily refer to in the context of this opening supplication?
A) The physical beginnings of the universe
B) The causes and principles of usul al-fiqh
C) The historical origins of Islamic law
D) The first few pages of the book

Key Takeaway
The opening supplication grounds the study of usul al-fiqh in tawhid: all principles and objectives are under Allah's control, and we rely solely on Him.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
7 min
The Completer of Wisdom: Salawat and the Prophet's Perfection
Commentary on the salawat and the description of the Prophet as completer of wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author follows praise of Allah with salawat upon the Prophet, and define 'hikmah' as it relates to the Prophet's mission.

Core Idea
The Prophet Muhammad was sent to complete wisdom, perfecting what previous prophets brought.

After praising Allah, the author sends blessings upon the Prophet. The commentator explains that this is because faith, the greatest blessing, came through the Prophet. The Prophet is described as 'the completer of wisdom' (al-mutammim li'l-hikam), alluding to the hadith 'I was sent to complete noble character.' In this lesson, we will explore the concept of hikmah and its completeness in the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure of the preface
The author first praises Allah, then sends salawat. The commentator explains the reason: gratitude for the greatest blessing (faith) which came via the Prophet.
2
Identify the allusion to the hadith
The phrase 'al-mutammim li'l-hikam' alludes to the hadith 'I was sent to complete noble character traits.'
This is a metaphorical attribution (isnad majazi).
3
Define hikmah
The commentator defines hikmah as knowledge of the real states of things, encompassing beliefs and ethics.
Hikmah has two types: theoretical (beliefs) and practical (character deeds).
4
Distinguish between complete and incomplete wisdom
Previous prophets had wisdom, but the Prophet Muhammad's wisdom is complete and perfect, as he perfected what was before.
This is based on the hadith 'I was sent to complete noble character.'
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Recognizing the Prophet as the completer of wisdom reinforces the authority of his Sunnah in deriving legal rulings.
His complete wisdom makes his teachings definitive.

قوله - اعنة المبادی بیدیک - اعنہ عنان کی جمع ہے اردو میں لگام کو کہتے ہیں مبادی، مبدا کی جمع ہے ہرشی کے اول کو یا جس پر اشیاء کا وجود موقوف ہو یعنی موقوف علیہ کو مبادی کہتے ہیں اس سے مراد اسباب ہیں۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اوامر و اسباب سب اللہ تعالی کے ہی پیدا کرنے سے ہیں وہ جو چاہتا ہے کرتا ہے اور جو چاہتا ہے حکم دیتا ہے اس سے اشارہ ہے آیت کریمہ فعال لما یرید کی طرف۔ مبادی سے یہاں پر خاص مبادی علوم بھی مراد لئے جاسکتے ہیں، خصوصاً مبادی اصول فقہ مراد لینا زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ اور ہرفن کے مبادی چونکہ اس فن کے مسائل ہوتے ہیں پس اس وقت عبارت کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ ہر فن خصوصاً اصول فقہ کے مبادی یعنی اس کے مسائل وقواعد تیرے ہی قبضہ واختیار میں ہیں جس کسی کو جو حاصل ہو گا تیرے ہی عطا کرنے سے حاصل ہوگا۔

قوله فانت المستعان وعليك التكلان : فاء تفريعية ہے، مستعان استعانت سے اسم مفعول ہے وہ ذات جس سے مدد مانگی جائے اس کو مستعان کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا قول تكلان اسم ہے تو كل کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور توكل ، اظہار بجز اور غير پر اعتماد کرنے کو کہتے ہیں معنی يہ ہے کہ اے ہمارے پروردگار ! جب تو ایسا ہے کہ مطالب و مقاصد اور مبادی واسباب سب تیرے ہی قبضہ واختیار میں میں اس لئے ہم تجھی پر بھروسہ کرتے ہیں اور تجھی سے مدد طلب کرتے ہیں مبادی واسباب سے مدد نہیں طلب کرتے کہ وہ از قبیل شرائط وروابط میں جو غیر مستقل اور خود محتاج ہوتے ہیں پس تیرے غیر پر کیسے بھروسہ کر سکتے ہیں۔
قوله والصلوة والسلام على سيدنا محمد ع الله : ۔ اللہ عز شانہ کے بندوں پر اتنے انعامات واحسانات ہیں جن کا حساب و شمار ممکن نہیں ارشا در بانی ہے فان تعدوها فلا تحصوها ۔ پس اس لئے اس کی غیر متناہی نعمتوں کے شکرانے میں حمد النہی بیان کیا، پھر دنیا کی ان تمام نعمتوں میں سب سے عظیم ترین وافضل نعمت ایمان ہے کہ اس پر اخروی حیات جاودانی اور اسکی کامیابی کا مدار ہے اور یہ عظیم دولت مسلمانوں کو پیغمبر اسلام ھادی اعظم نور مجسم حضرت محمد لے کے واسطہ سے ملی ہے تو ضروری ہو گیا کہ حمد الہی کے بعد فورا شکر ھادی ادا کیا جائے جیسا کہ آپ نے کا ارشاد ہے من لم يشكر الناس لم يشكر الله اس لئے حضرت مصنف نے حمد کے بعد صلوۃ وسلام پیش کیا اور تا کہ آیت يايها الذين امنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسلیما پر بھی عمل ہو جائے پس کہا والصلوة والسلام الخ
قوله المتمم للحكم: تميم سے اسم فاعل کا صیغہ ہے اکمال کے معنی میں ہے اس میں تلويح ہے حديث پاک بعثت لاتم مكارم الاخلاق کی طرف۔ اس میں اسناد مجازی ہے حکم جمع ہے حکمت کی ۔موجودات کے احوال واقعیہ ، بقدر طاقت بشر يہ جاننے کو حکمت کہتے ہیں، حکمت کی دو قسمیں ہیں حکمت نظریہ، حکمت عملیہ ۔ اول سے عقائد و اصول مراد ہیں اور نانی سے اخلاق مرضیہ واعمال صالحہ مراد ہیں اس لئے کہ حکمت کا اطلاق عدل و علم، حلم، نبوت، فقہ قرآن شریعت سب پر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے من يوتى الحكمة فقد اوتى خيراً كثيراً ۔ عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ حصور تے کو اللہ عز شانہ نے حکمت کے جملہ انواع و اقسام کا جامع اور تم بنا کر مبعوث کیا ہے حالانکہ پیشر وانبیاء کرام علیہم السلام کو بھی حکمتیں عطا کی گئیں تھیں تاہم وہ نامکمل تھیں مگر حضور سید تا آخرالزماں جاتا ہے کو حکمت تامہ کاملہ بالغہ عطا کی گئی اس لئے آپ نے فرمایا بعثت لاتمم مكارم الاخلاق
His statement: 'The reins of beginnings are in Your hand' — a'innah is the plural of inan, which in Urdu means 'reins'. Mabadi is the plural of mabda', meaning the beginning of something or that upon which the existence of things depends, i.e., the prerequisite; what is meant here are causes. The meaning is that commands and causes all are from the creation of Allah Almighty; He does what He wills and commands what He wills. This alludes to the noble verse 'Doer of whatever He intends'. Here, by 'beginnings' the beginnings of sciences can also be specifically intended, and it is more apparent to intend specifically the beginnings of usul al-fiqh. And since the beginnings of every discipline are the issues of that discipline, then the meaning of the expression is that the beginnings of every discipline, especially usul al-fiqh, i.e., its issues and rules, are in Your grasp and control; whoever obtains anything obtains it only from Your bestowal.
His statement: 'And the forelocks of objectives are entrusted to You' — nawasi is the plural of nasiyah, meaning the hair of the forehead or the end of where hair grows on all four sides. Maqasid is the plural of maqsad, meaning ‘intent.’ Mufawwadah is a feminine passive participle of tafwid, meaning ‘returned’ or ‘referred.’ In these two sentences, the manifest excellence, eloquence and rhetoric that the author has shown is not hidden from the attentive. It should be remembered that the author likened 'beginnings' (causes) to mounts that carry riders to the intended destination, but he did not mention the 'mounts' — the thing being likened — rather he only mentioned the 'beginnings' — the thing being likened — and mentioned from among the requisites of the thing-to-which-likened the 'reins'; in the art this style is called isti'arah bil-kinayah. Then, affirming 'reins' for 'beginnings' is isti'arah takhyiliyyah. Similarly, he likened the most important objectives — the difficult art and tangled issues — to wild, kicking animals that are hardly caught, and are controlled by catching their forelocks, but he did not mention the thing-to-which-likened; rather he mentioned from among its requisites the 'forelocks' — this also is isti'arah bil-kinayah; and then affirming 'forelocks' for 'objectives' is isti'arah takhyiliyyah.
His statement: 'For You are the One sought for help, and upon You is reliance' — the fa' is for detailing; musta'an is a passive participle from isti'anah, meaning the entity from whom help is sought. His word tuklan is a noun used in the sense of tawakkul, and tawakkul means expressing dependence on other than oneself. The meaning is: O our Lord! Since You are such that all requests and objectives, beginnings and causes are all in Your grasp and control, therefore we rely only on You and seek help only from You; we do not seek help from beginnings and causes, because they are of the category of conditions and means which are non-independent and themselves in need — so how can we rely on other than You?
His statement: 'And peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad' — Allah Almighty has so many favors and blessings upon His servants that counting them is impossible; as He said: 'If you count them, you cannot enumerate them.' Therefore, in gratitude for His endless blessings, the author expressed praise of Allah. Then, among all the blessings of this world, the greatest and most virtuous blessing is faith, upon which eternal life in the hereafter and its success depend; and this great wealth came to Muslims through the Prophet of Islam, the greatest guide, the embodied light, our master Muhammad, so it became necessary that after the praise of Allah, gratitude to the guide be expressed immediately, as the Prophet said: 'Whoever does not thank people has not thanked Allah.' Therefore, the author presented salawat and salam after the praise, and also to act upon the verse 'O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with salutations of peace.' So he said 'And peace and blessings...' etc.
His statement: 'The completer of wisdom' — it is the form of the active participle from tatmim, meaning completion. There is an allusion in it to the noble hadith: 'I was sent to complete the noble character traits.' This is a metaphorical attribution. Hikam is plural of hikmah. Knowing the real states of existing things to the extent of human capacity is called hikmah. There are two types of hikmah: theoretical wisdom and practical wisdom. The first refers to beliefs and principles, and the second refers to pleasing character and righteous deeds, because hikmah is applied to justice, knowledge, forbearance, prophethood, jurisprudence, the Quran, and the shariah. Thus the saying: 'Whoever is given hikmah has been given abundant good.' The meaning of the phrase is that the Prophet was sent by Allah Almighty as one who encompasses all types and kinds of hikmah, while previous prophets were also granted wisdoms, but they were incomplete; however, our master, the Seal of the Prophets, was granted complete, perfect, and mature wisdom. Therefore he said: 'I was sent to complete noble character traits.'
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the opening lines of the matn. The author, a Hanafi scholar, explains the metaphorical language used by the original author. First, 'the reins of beginnings are in Your hand' — 'reins' symbolizing control, and 'beginnings' meaning causes or the foundational principles. This affirms that all causes and commands are from Allah alone, alluding to the Quranic phrase 'Doer of whatever He intends.' The commentator notes that 'beginnings' can specifically refer to the principles of each science, especially usul al-fiqh, so the phrase means that the rules and principles of the science are under God's control. Next, 'the forelocks of objectives are entrusted to You' — 'forelocks' symbolize control like reins, and 'objectives' are the difficult goals of the science. The author uses a double metaphor: first likening causes to mounts (not explicitly mentioned) and objectives to wild animals, then mentioning only the reins and forelocks. This is identified as isti'arah bil-kinayah (metaphor by implication) and isti'arah takhyiliyyah (imaginary metaphor). Then the phrase 'For You are the One sought for help, and upon You is reliance' — explains that since everything is in God's hands, we only rely on Him, not on intermediate means. Then 'And peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad' — the commentator explains the structure of the author's preface: after praising God (not included here) for countless blessings, he sends blessings on the Prophet because faith is the greatest blessing and it came through him. This also fulfills the Quranic command to send salawat. Finally, 'the completer of wisdom' — the Prophet is described as the one who perfected wisdom, alluding to the hadith 'I was sent to complete noble character.' Wisdom (hikmah) is defined broadly as knowledge of realities, including beliefs and ethics. The commentator concludes that previous prophets had partial wisdom, but the Prophet Muhammad had complete wisdom, perfecting what came before.

Key Terms
حکمت (hikmah): Knowledge of the real states of existing things to the extent of human capacity; includes beliefs and ethics.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why does the author send blessings upon the Prophet immediately after praising Allah?
A) Because it is a requirement of the Quranic verse.
B) Because faith, the greatest blessing, came through the Prophet.
C) Because the Prophet is the source of all knowledge.
D) Because the author wants to show respect.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the completer of wisdom, sent to perfect noble character, making his Sunnah the complete source of guidance in usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding the Author's Invocation: Hamd, Salawat, and 'The Completer of Wisdom'
Commentary on the author's invocation and definition of a key term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of the author's praise and blessings in a Hanafi usul text and define the term 'al-mutammim li al-hukm' with its two types of wisdom.

Core Idea
The author's hamd and salawat are not formalities but express gratitude for faith through the Prophet, who completed all wisdom.

This passage opens a Hanafi usul work with praise to Allah and blessings upon the Prophet. The commentator unpacks why the author begins this way, linking it to the greatest blessing—faith—and the Prophet's role as the completer of wisdom. We will explore the logic behind the invocation and the definition of 'al-mutammim li al-hukm' as it relates to the Prophet's comprehensive mission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components of the invocation
The author begins with hamd (praise of Allah) followed by salawat (blessings upon the Prophet). Note that the commentator justifies this order.
2
Analyze the reason for hamd
The commentator states that Allah's bounties are countless, so hamd is an expression of gratitude. Understand the link between gratitude and the inability to enumerate blessings (Quran 16:18).
The verse 'If you count them, you cannot enumerate them' is cited.
3
Analyze the reason for salawat
The greatest blessing among worldly blessings is faith, which comes through the Prophet. Hence, after praising Allah, gratitude must be shown to the Prophet via salawat. The commentator also cites the hadith 'He who does not thank people does not thank Allah' and the Quranic command to send blessings (33:56).
This shows the necessity of thanking the intermediary of divine favor.
4
Deconstruct the term 'al-mutammim li al-hukm'
'al-mutammim' means 'the completer', and 'hukm' is the plural of 'hikmah' (wisdom). Wisdom is defined as knowledge of the real states of existent things to the extent of human capability.
The term alludes to the hadith 'I was sent to complete the noble traits of character.'
5
Distinguish the two types of wisdom
Wisdom is divided into theoretical (beliefs, principles) and practical (praiseworthy morals, righteous deeds). The Prophet was sent as the comprehensive embodiment of both, perfecting what earlier prophets had incompletely received.
This establishes the Prophet's unique status in conveying complete guidance.

Source Text

قوله والصلوة والسلام على سيدنا محمد ع الله : ۔ اللہ عز شانہ کے بندوں پر اتنے انعامات واحسانات ہیں جن کا حساب و شمار ممکن نہیں ارشاد باری ہے فان تعدوها فلا تحصوها ۔ پس اس لئے اس کی غیر متناہی نعمتوں کے شکرانے میں حمد الہی بیان کیا، پھر دنیا کی ان تمام نعمتوں میں سب سے عظیم ترین وافضل نعمت ایمان ہے کہ اس پر اخروی حیات جاودانی اور اسکی کامیابی کا مدار ہے اور یہ عظیم دولت مسلمانوں کو پیغمبر اسلام ھادی اعظم نور مجسم حضرت محمد صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے واسطہ سے ملی ہے تو ضروری ہو گیا کہ حمد الہی کے بعد فورا شکر ھادی ادا کیا جائے جیسا کہ آپ نے کا ارشاد ہے من لم يشكر الناس لم يشكر الله اس لئے حضرت مصنف نے حمد کے بعد صلوۃ وسلام پیش کیا اور تا کہ آیت يايها الذين امنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسلیما پر بھی عمل ہو جائے پس کہا والصلوة والسلام الخ
قوله المتمم للحكم: تمیم سے اسم فاعل کا صیغہ ہے اکمال کے معنی میں ہے اس میں تلویح ہے حدیث پاک بعثت لاتمم مکارم الاخلاق کی طرف۔ اس میں اسناد مجازی ہے حکم جمع ہے حکمت کی ۔موجودات کے احوال واقعیہ ، بقدر طاقت بشر یہ جاننے کو حکمت کہتے ہیں، حکمت کی دو قسمیں ہیں حکمت نظریہ، حکمت عملیہ ۔ اول سے عقائد و اصول مراد ہیں اور ثانی سے اخلاق مرضیہ واعمال صالحہ مراد ہیں اس لئے کہ حکمت کا اطلاق عدل و علم، حلم، نبوت، فقہ قرآن شریعت سب پر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے من يوتى الحكمة فقد اوتى خيراً كثيراً ۔ عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو اللہ عز شانہ نے حکمت کے جملہ انواع و اقسام کا جامع اور کامل بنا کر مبعوث کیا ہے حالانکہ پیشرو انبیاء کرام علیہم السلام کو بھی حکمتیں عطا کی گئیں تھیں تاہم وہ نامکمل تھیں مگر حضور سید الانبیاء علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کو حکمت تامہ کاملہ بالغہ عطا کی گئی اس لئے آپ نے فرمایا بعثت لاتمم مكارم الاخلاق
That, O our Lord! Since You are such that all objectives and purposes, and all beginnings and causes are in Your grip and control, therefore we trust only in You and seek help only from You, not from causes and means, because they are of the category of conditions and connections that are non-independent and themselves in need. So how can we trust in other than You?
His statement: 'And prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad' may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Allah, Exalted is His glory, has so many favors and bounties upon His servants that their count is not possible. His command is: 'If you count them, you cannot enumerate them.' Therefore, in gratitude for His infinite blessings, praise of Allah was expressed. Then, among all these worldly blessings, the greatest and most excellent blessing is faith, upon which depends eternal life in the Hereafter and its success. And this great wealth came to Muslims through the intermediary of the Prophet of Islam, the greatest guide, embodied light, Hadrat Muhammad (peace be upon him). So it became necessary that after praising Allah, gratitude should be immediately expressed to the guide, as the Prophet said: 'He who does not thank people does not thank Allah.' Therefore, the author presented prayers and peace after praise, and also to act upon the verse: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him and greet him with greetings of peace.' So he said: 'And prayers and peace' etc.
His statement: 'The completer of wisdom.' It is the form of the active participle from 'tamim', meaning completion. In this there is an allusion to the noble hadith: 'I was sent to complete the noble traits of character.' In it there is a metaphorical attribution. 'Hukm' is the plural of 'hikmah'. Knowing the real states of existent things to the extent of human capability is called wisdom. Wisdom is of two types: theoretical wisdom and practical wisdom. From the first are meant beliefs and principles, and from the second are meant praiseworthy morals and righteous deeds. Because wisdom is applied to justice, knowledge, forbearance, prophethood, jurisprudence, the Qur'an, and all of Sharia. Thus He said: 'Whoever is given wisdom has been given abundant good.' The meaning of the phrase is that the Messenger (peace be upon him) was sent by Allah, Exalted is His glory, as the comprehensive and perfect one of all types and kinds of wisdom. Although previous noble prophets (peace be upon them) were also given wisdom, yet it was incomplete. But the Master of the prophets (peace and blessings be upon him) was given complete, perfect, and mature wisdom. Therefore he said: 'I was sent to complete the noble traits of character.'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening phrases of the book 'Muslim al-Thubut'. The commentator, writing in Urdu, explains the rationale behind the author's invocation of praise (hamd) and blessings (salawat) upon the Prophet. He argues that since all means and causes are dependent on God, trust should be placed solely in Him. Then he explains that the greatest blessing after God's praise is faith, which came through the Prophet, necessitating gratitude through blessings. He then defines the term 'al-mutammim li al-hukm' (the completer of wisdom). He notes that 'hukm' is plural of 'hikmah' (wisdom), and wisdom is knowledge of the realities of things. Wisdom is divided into theoretical (beliefs and principles) and practical (morals and deeds). The Prophet Muhammad was sent as the perfect embodiment of all forms of wisdom, completing the partial wisdom given to previous prophets, as indicated by the hadith 'I was sent to complete the noble traits of character.' The commentary thus establishes the Prophet's unique status as the perfect teacher and exemplar.

Key Terms
المتمم للحكم (al-mutammim li al-hukm): The one who completes wisdom; referring to the Prophet as perfecting all forms of wisdom
حکمت (hikmah): Knowledge of the real states of existent things to the extent of human capability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why does the author mention 'al-mutammim li al-hukm' (the completer of wisdom) in relation to the Prophet?
A) Because the Prophet was the first to receive wisdom
B) Because the Prophet perfected all types of wisdom, completing what earlier prophets had received incompletely
C) Because wisdom is only given to prophets
D) Because the Prophet was the wisest among his people

Key Takeaway
The author's invocation is a deliberate expression of gratitude for the greatest blessing (faith) through the Prophet, who is described as the completer of all wisdom.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Resolving Ambiguity in 'al-Arbaʿat al-Uṣūl': Proofs for the Intellects
Commentary expanding the opening duʿā' and resolving ambiguity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Rawāfiḍ and Ahl al-Sunnah interpretations of 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' and explain how the commentator uses the term to allude to the four sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh.

Core Idea
The four caliphs are proofs for intellects; 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' bridges historical figures and Uṣūl al-Fiqh's four sources.

This lesson examines a commentary passage where the author's salutation to the Prophet's family and companions is interpreted. The phrase 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' creates an ambiguity: does it refer to the Prophet's household (Āl) or the Companions (Aṣḥāb)? The commentator resolves this in favor of Ahl al-Sunnah, and further reveals a subtle allusion to the four foundational sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh: the Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase and its two possible referents
The phrase 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' (the four principles) occurs after mentioning the Prophet's family and companions. One reading takes it as a description of 'āl' (family), making it refer to ʿAlī, Ḥasan, Ḥusayn, and Fāṭima. The other reading takes it as a description of 'aṣḥāb' (companions), making it refer to the four Rightly Guided Caliphs.
The Rawāfiḍ adhere to the first reading; Ahl al-Sunnah to the second.
2
Analyze the commentator's criteria for tarjīḥ (preponderance)
The commentator notes that the word 'sayyumā' (especially) connects naturally to 'aṣḥāb' both linguistically and in context. Moreover, the author's known affiliation with Ahl al-Sunnah confirms the interpretation as the four caliphs. This illustrates how grammar and authorial intent resolve textual ambiguity.
The principle: al-aṣl fī al-kalām al-ḥaqīqah (the default is literal meaning) but here context overrides.
3
Appreciate the dual allusion: caliphs and usul sources
The commentator points out that by using 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' instead of naming the caliphs, the author alludes to the four sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh (Kitāb, Sunnah, Ijmāʿ, Qiyās). This demonstrates a literary technique called barāʿat al-istihlāl (ingenuous opening), signaling the subject of the work.
This depth of interpretation is characteristic of learned commentaries (shurūḥ).
4
Connect to the overall discipline of Uṣūl al-Fiqh
The salutation thus serves a dual purpose: honoring the companions and introducing the four foundational proofs that will be discussed in the book. Understanding this helps students recognize how classical scholars embedded methodological points in seemingly routine phrases.
This passage is a microcosm of the entire work: the four caliphs as proofs for intellects mirror the four proofs of jurisprudence.

Source Text

تا کہ لوگ اس پر عمل پیرا ہوسکیں۔
صاحب الخصوص نے کہا ہے کہ جوامع الکلم سے وہ کلمات مراد ہیں جو صفات الہیہ کو جامع ہیں تا کہ دعوت و تبلیغ سے پہلے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اخلاق خداوندی سے متخلق ہونا سمجھا جائے اور آپ کی دعوت کے کا حقیقتا اللہ تعالی ہی کی دعوت ہونے کا شعور ہو۔
قوله وعلى آله واصحابه الذين هم ادلة العقول - الخ اس کا قول ادلہ دلیل کی جمع ہے یہاں اس سے مراد الموصل الى المطلوب یا من مرشد السبل ہے عقول، عقل کی جمع ہے عقل لغت میں قید کو کہتے ہیں کہا جاتا ہے عقلت البعيرای قیدة ، ۔ پھر چند معانی کی طرف عقل کو منتقل کر لیا گیا ، یہاں مراد وہ ادراک ہے جس کے ذریعہ انسان بہائم سے ممتاز ہوتا ہے۔ اصطلاح میں عقل نفس کی اس قوت کا نام ہے جس کے ذریعہ روح مبدا فیاض کی طرف سے عطا کردہ علوم و ادراکات کے حصول کے لئے مستعد رہے ۔ سیما ، میں مازائدہ یا موصوفہ ہے اور اسی مثل کے معنی میں آتا ہے مگر بطور استثناء خصوصاً “ کے معنی میں استعمال ہونے لگا اس کا قول الا ربعہ الاصول اگر آل کی صفت ہے تو اس سے امیر المومنین امام المتقین حضرت علی ابن ابی طالب، آپ کے دونوں پھول حضرات حسنین کریمین اور حضرت سيدة نساء الجنۃ فاطمتہ الزہرا مراد ہیں جیسا کہ رفضہ کا گمان ہے اور اگر اصحاب کی صفت ہے تو اس سے خلفاء راشدین حضرت ابو بکر وعمر وعثمان وعلی رضوان اللہ تعالیٰ علیہم اجمعین مراد ہیں۔ یہی زیادہ راجح ، واضح اور ظاہر ہے کہ مصنف اہل سنت و جماعت سے ہیں رفضہ سے نہیں نیز سیما سے استثناء و اختصاص ، آل سے نہیں بلکہ اصحاب سے ہے کہ سیما کا تعلق اصحاب سے لفظا معنا انسب ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ حضور میں لینے کے آل و اصحاب خصوصاً حضرات خلفاء اربعہ مومنین کی عقلوں کی دلیلیں ہیں اور دلیل کا کام راستہ دکھانا و مطلوب تک پہونچانا ہوتا ہے ظاہر ہے کہ مسلمانوں نے ایمان و اسلام اور رشد و ہدایت کا جو راہ مستقیم دیکھا ہے وہ انہیں حضرات صحابہ خصوصاً خلفاء راشدین رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کی مرہون منت ہے۔ اس میں اشارہ ہے ”حدیث ان اصحابی کالنجوم بايهم اقتديتم اهتديتم - وعليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدین کی طرف۔ کمالا يخفى على من له ادنى تامل ۔ خلفاء اربعہ کے اسماء کے بجائے الاربعة الاصول استعمال کیا کہ اس میں موضوع اصول فقہ، کتاب سنت و اجماع و قیاس کی طرف براعت استبلال کے طور پر اشارہ کرنا ہے۔
So that people may act upon it. The author of al-Khusūs said that by 'comprehensive speech' (jawāmi‘ al-kalim) is meant the words that encompass divine attributes, so that before calling and preaching, the Prophet's (ﷺ) character being imbued with divine morality may be understood, and it may be realized that his call is in reality God's call. His statement: 'And upon his family and companions who are the proofs of intellects' – his saying 'adilla' is the plural of 'dalīl'; here it means that which leads to the desired end or the guide of paths. 'Uqūl' is the plural of 'aql'; 'aql' lexically means restraint; it is said 'aqaltu al-baʿīra' i.e., I restrained it. Then it was transferred to several meanings; here it means that perception through which man is distinguished from animals. Terminologically, 'aql' is the name of that faculty of the soul by which the spirit is prepared to acquire the sciences and perceptions granted by the First Bestower. 'Sayyumā' is an extra or descriptive word and it comes in the meaning of 'like', but as an exception it came to be used in the sense of 'especially'. His statement 'except the four principles' (illā arbaʿata uṣūl) – if it is a description of 'āl' (family), then it refers to the Commander of the Faithful, the Imam of the Pious, ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib, his two flowers al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, and the Chief of the Women of Paradise Fāṭima al-Zahrā', as the Rawāfiḍ think. And if it is a description of 'aṣḥāb' (companions), then it refers to the Rightly Guided Caliphs, Abū Bakr, ʿUmar, ʿUthmān, and ʿAlī, may God be pleased with them all. This is more preponderant, clear, and apparent, that the author is from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamāʿah, not from the Rawāfiḍ. Also, 'sayyumā' is for exception and specification, not of 'āl' but of 'aṣḥāb', because the connection of 'sayyumā' with 'aṣḥāb' is more appropriate in wording and meaning. The meaning is: the Prophet's (ﷺ) family and companions, especially the four caliphs, are the proofs of the believers' intellects, and the function of a proof is to show the way and reach the desired end. It is apparent that the straight path of faith, Islam, guidance, and direction that Muslims have seen is indebted to these esteemed companions, especially the Rightly Guided Caliphs. In this is an allusion to the hadith: 'My companions are like stars; whichever of them you follow, you will be guided,' and 'Follow my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.' This is no secret to anyone with the slightest reflection. Instead of the names of the four caliphs, he used 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' to allude to the subject of Uṣūl al-Fiqh, and to the Book, Sunnah, Ijmaʿ, and Qiyās by way of opening excellence.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's opening salutation (salāt and salām) to the Prophet and his family and companions. The commentator explains the phrase 'adillat al-ʿuqūl' (proofs of intellects) in detail. He notes that 'adilla' means proofs that lead to the desired end, and 'ʿuqūl' refers to the faculty of discernment that distinguishes humans from animals. He then discusses the tricky phrase 'illā arbaʿata uṣūl' (except the four principles). The commentator clarifies that the Rawāfiḍ (Rafidites) mistakenly interpret this as referring to ʿAlī, Ḥasan, Ḥusayn, and Fāṭima (as a description of 'āl'), but the correct interpretation according to Ahl al-Sunnah is that it refers to the four Rightly Guided Caliphs (as a description of 'aṣḥāb'). The commentator asserts that the author is from Ahl al-Sunnah, and the word 'sayyumā' (especially) here connects to 'aṣḥāb', not 'āl'. He explains that the companions, especially the four caliphs, are proofs that guide believers to the straight path. He also references the famous hadith about following the companions and the caliphs. Finally, he notes the elegance of using 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' instead of names, as it alludes to the four sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the subject of the book itself.

Key Terms
آل (āl): Family of the Prophet, specifically here referring to his household (ʿAlī, Ḥasan, Ḥusayn, Fāṭima) according to the Rawāfiḍ, but in the correct interpretation it is not the referent of 'sayyumā'.
اصحاب (aṣḥāb): Companions of the Prophet, especially the four Rightly Guided Caliphs, who are intended here as the 'proofs of intellects'.
الاربعة الاصول (al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl): The four principles: the four Rightly Guided Caliphs (by interpretation), but also alluding to the four sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh: Kitāb, Sunnah, Ijmāʿ, Qiyās.
ادلة العقول (adillat al-ʿuqūl): Proofs for the intellects; the companions and caliphs act as proofs that guide the intellects of the believers to the truth.
سيما (sayyumā): Especially; used here for exception and specification, connecting to 'aṣḥāb'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct interpretation of 'الاربعة الاصول' in this passage?
A) It refers to the Prophet's family (Āl): ʿAlī, Ḥasan, Ḥusayn, and Fāṭima.
B) It refers to the four Rightly Guided Caliphs and also alludes to the four sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh.
C) It refers to the four founders of the Islamic schools of thought.
D) It refers to the four major companions: ʿAlī, ʿUmar, ʿUthmān, and Abū Bakr without any other allusion.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'al-arbaʿat al-uṣūl' in the salutation simultaneously honors the four caliphs and alludes to the four foundational sources of Uṣūl al-Fiqh.
