Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Purpose and Scope of Muslim al-Thubut
Opening of the matn of Muslim al-Thubut by the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the aims, structure, and unique comparative approach of Muslim al-Thubut as stated in its introduction.

Core Idea
Muslim al-Thubut combines Hanafi and Shafi'i usul methods without deviating from reality.

The author, Muhibb Allah ibn Abd al-Shakur, opens his seminal usul text, Muslim al-Thubut, with a classical introduction that sets forth the work's purpose and methodology. Understanding this introduction is crucial because it defines the book's comparative framework—a synthesis of Hanafi and Shafi'i principles grounded in both revelation and reason. This lesson unpacks the author's stated aims and the significance of his approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's motivation
Read how the author describes his personal journey in studying usul al-fiqh and his desire to compile a comprehensive work that combines branches (furu') with principles (usul).
The author claims mastery after extensive study, then decides to write a book that integrates both the revealed (mashru') and the rational (ma'qul).
2
Recognize the comparative dimension
Notice the explicit statement that the book contains both the methods of the Hanafis and the Shafi'is (يحتوى على طريقى الحنفية والشافعية). This shows the work is not limited to one madhhab.
The phrase 'without inclining away from reality' (ولايميل ميلا ما عن الواقعية) indicates a commitment to objective truth over partisan bias.
3
Understand the naming and its significance
The author names his work 'al-Muslim' and later reveals the inspired date-title 'Muslim al-Thubut'. Reflect on why 'Muslim' (the one who submits/peace) and 'al-Thubut' (firmness, certainty) are chosen.
The title suggests the work is a safe, authoritative source that provides firm proofs (thubut) for usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما بعد فيقول الشكور الصبور محب الله بن عبدالشكور بلغه الله تعالى الى ذروة الكمال ورقاه عن حضيض القال الى قلة الحال أن السعادة باستكمال النفس والمادة وذالك بالتحقق والتخلق وهما بالتفقه في الدين والتبـحـر بـمـوافـق الحق واليقين والسلوك فى هذا الودى انما يتاتى بتحصيل المبادى ومنها علم اصول الاحكام فهو من أجل علوم الاسلام الف في مدحه خطب وصنف في قواعده كتب وكنت صرفت بعض عمرى الى تحصيل مطالبه ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق مأربه فلم يحتجب عنى حقيقة ولم يخف على دقيقة ثم لامرما اردت أن أحررفيه سفراً وافياً وكتاباً كافياً يجمع الى الفروع اصولا والى المشروع معقولا ويحتوى على طريقى الحنفية والشافعية ولايميل ميلا ما عن الواقعية فجاء بفضل الله تعالى وتوفيقه کماتری معدن ام بحر بل سحر لايدرى وسميته بالمسلم سلمه الله تعالى عن الطرح والجرح وجعله موجباً للسرور والفرح ثم ألهمنى مالك الملكوت أن تاريخه مسلم الثبوت
Now then, says the grateful and patient servant, Muḥibb Allāh ibn ʿAbd al-Shakūr — may Allāh, Most High, elevate him to the summit of perfection and raise him from the pit of 'they said' to the height of spiritual state — that happiness (saʿādah) lies in the perfection of the soul and the physical constitution, and that is by verification (taḥaqquq) and moral adornment (takhalluq), and these two are through deep understanding in religion (tafaqquh fī al-dīn) and being versed in what agrees with truth and certainty. And entering this valley is only possible by acquiring the principles (mabādī), among which is the science of the foundations of rulings (ʿilm uṣūl al-aḥkām). It is one of the most noble of Islamic sciences; sermons have been composed in its praise and books authored on its principles. I spent part of my life in seeking its subjects and devoted my gaze to achieving its goals, so no reality was veiled from me and no subtle point remained hidden. Then, due to a command, I desired to compile a comprehensive volume and a sufficient book that combines branches with principles and the legislated with the rational, and contains both the methods of the Ḥanafīs and the Shāfiʿīs, without inclining away from reality. By the grace and success of Allāh, it came out as you see — a mine, nay a sea, nay indescribable magic. I named it 'al-Muslim' — may Allāh protect it from rejection and criticism, and make it a cause of delight and joy. Then the Possessor of the Kingdom inspired me that its date (history) is 'Muslim al-Thubūt'.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the matn (original text) of Muslim al-Thubut by Muhibb Allah ibn Abd al-Shakur. It is a typical author's introduction (khutbah al-kitab). The author begins by praising Allah and stating his purpose. He defines happiness as perfecting both soul and body through verification of truth and moral adornment, which are achieved by deep understanding of religion (tafaqquh fi al-din) and being thoroughly grounded in what is correct. He then states that entering the path of this knowledge requires mastering its preliminary sciences, among which is 'ilm usul al-ahkam (the science of uṣūl al-fiqh). He praises this science as one of the noblest. He then recounts his personal journey: he spent much of his life studying and researching usul al-fiqh, attaining mastery. Then he decided to write a comprehensive book that would bring together both the substantive rulings (furu') and the principles (usul), and incorporate both the Shar' (revealed law) and reason (ma'qul). Importantly, he states that the book contains both the methods of the Hanafis and the Shafi'is, without deviating from reality. This indicates that his work is comparative but remains grounded in the actual practice. He then describes the result as a mine or sea of knowledge, and names it 'al-Muslim'. Then he says that the title was inspired as 'Muslim al-Thubut' (meaning 'the firm proof' or 'the certain one'), which is the name of the book. This introduction sets the stage for a comprehensive usul text that aims to synthesize different madhhab approaches while remaining faithful to the truth.

Key Terms
سعادة (saʿādah): Happiness in both worlds, achieved by perfecting the soul and body through knowledge and action.
استكمال النفس (istikmāl al-nafs): Perfection of the soul through acquiring knowledge and virtues.
تفقه في الدين (tafaqquh fī al-dīn): Deep understanding of religion, particularly in matters of fiqh and usul.
علم اصول الاحكام (ʿilm uṣūl al-aḥkām): The science of the foundations of legal rulings; i.e., Uṣūl al-Fiqh.
مسلم الثبوت (Muslim al-Thubūt): The title of the book, meaning 'the firm proof' or 'the certain one', alluding to its authoritative status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the unique feature of Muslim al-Thubut according to its introduction?
A) It only discusses Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
B) It combines both Hanafi and Shafi'i methods without deviating from reality.
C) It is a commentary on a previous work.
D) It focuses only on rational proofs ignoring transmitted evidence.

Key Takeaway
Muslim al-Thubut is distinguished by its comparative methodology, presenting both Hanafi and Shafi'i usul principles while remaining committed to objective truth.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Author's Introduction to Muslim al-Thubut
Author's preface explaining book's purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose and scope of the book Muslim al-Thubut and identify its significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Muslim al-Thubut unites Hanafi and Shafi'i usul without bias, aiming for firm proofs.

In this opening passage, the author Muhibb Allah ibn Abd al-Shakur lays out his motivation and methodology for writing Muslim al-Thubut. Understanding this preface is essential to appreciating the work's unique position in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's self-description
The author calls himself 'al-Shakur al-Sabur' (the grateful patient one). Note that this is metaphorical, not literal, and relates to Quranic attributes.
This establishes the author's humility and spiritual aspirations.
2
Understand the purpose of the book
The author states that true happiness (sa'ada) comes from perfecting the soul through deep understanding of religion, which requires knowledge of usul al-ahkam (legal principles). This book aims to be a comprehensive guide to usul.
Usul al-ahkam is the science of deriving rulings, i.e., usul al-fiqh.
3
Note the scope: Hanafi and Shafi'i schools
The author explicitly says the book encompasses the ways of the Hanafis and Shafi'is without inclining away from reality. This makes it a unique comparative work.
Most usul works focus on one school; this one bridges two major schools.
4
Recognize the title and its inspiration
The book is named 'al-Muslim' (the safe one), and later inspired to be called 'Muslim al-Thubut' (the firm in proof). This indicates the author's hope for acceptance and the work's reliability.
The title itself reflects the book's purpose: to provide firm proofs in usul.
5
Appreciate the book as a memorization anchor
As a foundational text in Hanafi usul, Muslim al-Thubut serves as a 'memorization anchor' — a concise yet comprehensive matn that students commit to memory and then study with commentaries.
This passage introduces the text that will be the basis for the rest of the course.

Source Text

أما بعد فيقول الشكور الصبور محب الله بن عبدالشكور بلغه الله تعالى الى ذروة الكمال ورقاه عن حضيض القال الى قلة الحال أن السعادة باستكمال النفس والمادة وذالك بالتحقق والتخلق وهما بالتفقه في الدين والتبـحـر بـمـوافـق الحق واليقين والسلوك فى هذا الودى انما يتاتى بتحصيل المبادى ومنها علم اصول الاحكام فهو من أجل علوم الاسلام الف في مدحه خطب وصنف في قواعده كتب وكنت صرفت بعض عمرى الى تحصيل مطالبه ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق مأربه فلم يحتجب عنى حقيقة ولم يخف على دقيقة ثم لامرما اردت أن أحررفيه سفراً وافياً وكتاباً كافياً يجمع الى الفروع اصولا والى المشروع معقولا ويحتوى على طريقى الحنفية والشافعية ولايميل ميلا ما عن الواقعية فجاء بفضل الله تعالى وتوفيقه كماتری معدن ام بحر بل سحر لايدرى وسميته بالمسلم سلمه الله تعالى عن الطرح والجرح وجعله موجباً للسرور والفرح ثم ألهمنى مالك الملكوت أن تاريخه مسلم الثبوت
ترجمه : پس ، حمد و صلوۃ کے بعد صابر و شاکر بندہ محب اللہ بن عبد الشکور، اللہ تعالی اس کو درجہ کمال کی بلندی پر پہونچائے اور پستی مقال سے نکال کر حال کی چوٹی پر چڑھائے ( آمین ) عرض کرتا ہے کہ دنیا و آخرت کی سعادت جسم و روح کو معارف الہیہ کے ذریعہ آراستہ کرنے سے دامل ہوتی ہے اور استکمال نفس عقائد اسلامیہ کے یقین و پختگی اور اعمال صالحہ سے مزین و آراستگی سے پیدا ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ دونوں چیزیں تفقہ فی الدین اور مقامات حق ویقین میں تبجحر حاصل کرنے سے پیدا ہوتی ہیں۔ اور اس وادی میں قدم رکھنا مبادیات کے حاصل کرنے کے بعد ہی ممکن ہے۔ مبادی فقہ میں سے ایک علم اصول احکام ہے بیشک وہ علوم اسلامیہ میں ایک ایسا عظیم و جلیل علم ہے جس کی تعریف میں خطبے پڑھے گئے اور جن کے قواعد کے بیان میں بہت سی کتابیں تحریر کی گئیں چنانچہ میں نے اپنی زندگی کا ایک عرصہ اسی اصول فقہ کے مطالب کے حاصل کرنے میں لگا دیا اور اس کے مقاصد کی تحقیق میں میں نے اپنی قوت نظریہ کو پھیر دیا پس مجھ سے اس فن کی کوئی حقیقت چھپی نہ رہ سکی اور مجھ سے اس کا کوئی راز سر بستہ نہ رہا، پھر ایک امر عظیم کے باعث میں نے اس فن میں ایک بڑا دفتر یا ایسی کتاب کی تصنیف کا ارادہ کر لیا جو اصول فقہ کے طلبہ کے لئے کافی ہو، احکام فقہیہ کے ساتھ دلائل پر اور امور شرعیہ مشتمل ہو اور حنفی و شافعی دونوں مذاہب کو جامع اور محیط ہو اور حقیقت واقعیہ سے کے ساتھ امور عقلیہ پر ذرہ برابر الگ نہ ہوپس اللہ تعالیٰ کے فضل و کرم اور اسکی توفیق رفیق سے زیر نظر کتاب معرض وجود میں آگئی جو ایک علمی جواہر کا خزانہ ہے یا علم کی موتیوں کا سمندر ہے بلکہ وہ ایک ایسا جادو ہے جسکی حقیقت کا پستہ نہیں ۔ اور میں نے اس کا نام مسلم رکھا ہے تا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اس کو غیر مقبول ہونے اور طعن و تشنیع سے محفوظ وسلاست رکھے اور اس کو مسرت و شادمانی کا سامان بنادے، پھر مالک الملکوت کی طرف سے مجھکو الہام ہوا کہ اس کا تاریخی نام مسلم الثبوت ہے شاھ تشريح : قوله - الشكور الصبور - یہ دونوں کلے بظاہر مبالغہ کے صیغے ہیں مگر یہاں مجاز أصابر و شاکر کے معنی میں استعمال کئے گئے ہیں۔ جیسا کہ قرآن حکیم میں ارشاد ہوا ليريكم من آياته ان في ذالك لآيات لكل صبار شكور ، شاکر کے بجائے الشكور استعمال کیا اس کی کئی وجہیں ہو سکتی ہیں (۱) تاکہ بعد میں آنے والے لفظ عبد الشكور کے ساتھ صنعت تجنیس کی رعایت ہو سکے ، اسی طرح صابر کے بجائے الصبور اس لئے کہا تا کہ جمع کی رعایت برقرار ہے۔ (۲) شکوراس لئے ذکر کیا تا کہ اللہ عز شانہ کے ارشاد و قليل من عبادی الشكور میں جن صابر و شاکر خاصگان خدا اور مقربین بارگاہ کا تذکرہ ہے انہیں مقربین بارگاہ کی طرح مصنف بھی صابر وشا کر ہو جا ئیں اور صابر کے بجائے صبور بھی اسی لئے کہا تا کہ شکور کے ساتھ تجنیس ہو سکے (۳) صفت شکور وصور استعمال کرنے کی وجہ بیان کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔ الوصف الاول كانه بالارث وذالك لان عبد كل اسم يكون له حظ من ذالك الاسم والوصف الثانى بنفسه لان اللائق بحال المحب الصبر على البلاء بناءً على أن الاسماء تتنزل من السماء انتهت
To proceed: The grateful patient one, Muhibb Allah ibn Abd al-Shakur, may Allah the Exalted elevate him to the peak of perfection and raise him from the lowliness of [mere] speech to the summit of [spiritual] state, [states:] Verily, happiness lies in the perfection of the soul and the body, and that is through verification and moral adornment, and both are attained through deep understanding of religion and immersion in what conforms to truth and certainty. Traversing this valley is only possible by acquiring the preliminary sciences, among which is the science of legal principles (usul al-ahkam). It is among the noblest of Islamic sciences. Sermons have been composed in its praise and books written on its rules. I devoted part of my life to acquiring its subjects and focused my sight on investigating its aims. No reality was veiled from me, nor was any subtlety hidden. Then, for an important reason, I intended to compile a comprehensive volume and a sufficient book that gathers principles with branches and rational proofs with legal matters, encompassing the ways of the Hanafis and Shafi'is without inclining away from reality. By the grace and success of Allah the Exalted, it emerged as you see: a mine, a sea, rather an indescribable sorcery. I named it 'al-Muslim' (the safe one), may Allah protect it from rejection and criticism, and make it a cause of joy and happiness. Then the Owner of the Dominion inspired me that its date [name] is 'Muslim al-Thubut'.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his book al-Muslim al-Thubut. It follows the classical structure: after the basmala and hamdala, the author begins with 'amma ba'd' (to proceed). He identifies himself as al-Shakur al-Sabur (the grateful patient one) – though these are forms of exaggeration, he uses them metaphorically as per the commentary. He explains that true happiness (sa'ada) comes from perfecting the soul and body through verification (tahaqquq) and moral adornment (takhalluq), which are achieved by deep understanding of the religion (tafaqquh fi al-din) and immersion in truth. The path to this requires learning the preliminary sciences, among which is 'ilm usul al-ahkam (the science of legal principles), the noblest of Islamic sciences. The author states he devoted his life to this field, mastered it, and then decided to write a comprehensive book that combines usul (principles) with furu' (branches), and rational proofs with revealed texts, covering both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools without bias. By Allah's grace, the book was completed and he named it 'al-Muslim' meaning 'the safe one', hoping for divine protection. He then mentions that the date of completion gave the title 'Muslim al-Thubut' (the safe/firm in proof). The Urdu translation and commentary (tashrih) elaborate on the meanings of the words al-Shakur and al-Sabur, explaining that they are used metaphorically to align with Quranic usage and to create literary harmony (tajnis). The commentator also notes that authors have a share in the names they use.

Key Terms
اصول الاحكام (usul al-ahkam): The science of legal principles (usul al-fiqh) from which the rulings of Islamic law are derived.
مسلم الثبوت (Muslim al-Thubut): The title of the book, meaning 'the safe/firm in proof', indicating its reliability in establishing legal principles.
شكور صبور (shakur sabur): Metaphorical descriptors used by the author: 'grateful patient one', based on Quranic attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author name his book 'al-Muslim'?
A) It was his teacher's name
B) To express hope that Allah would protect it from criticism and make it a cause of joy
C) Because the book covers only Muslim views
D) Because he was a Muslim

Key Takeaway
The author intended Muslim al-Thubut to be a comprehensive, unbiased usul work bridging Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, with a title reflecting its firm proofs.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Author's Self-Description and Opening Prayer
Author's self-description and opening prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author called himself al-Shakur al-Sabur and interpret the opening supplication in light of Hanafi usul al-fiqh tradition.

Core Idea
A name carries barakah and effect; the author's attributes stem from his father's name and his own name Muhibb Allah.

This passage opens the commentary on Muslim al-Thubut with the author's self-introduction and a prayer. The author, Muhibb Allah ibn 'Abd al-Shakur, describes himself as 'al-Shakur al-Sabur'. The commentator unpacks these attributes, revealing how they connect to his father's name and his own. Understanding this helps us appreciate the author's spiritual lineage and the seriousness with which he approaches his work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's attributes
Locate the two attributes the author uses for himself: al-Shakur and al-Sabur. Note that these are divine attributes, but here they are applied to a human author in a specific, justified sense.
Al-Shakur is one of Allah's names, al-Sabur is also an attribute of Allah.
2
Trace the basis for 'al-Shakur'
Understand the reasoning: the author's father was named 'Abd al-Shakur, so the attribute 'Shakur' comes to the author by inheritance, as the son is the secret and heir of his father.
The principle 'al-waladu sirru abihi' (the son is the secret of his father) is invoked.
3
Trace the basis for 'al-Sabur'
The author's own name is Muhibb Allah (Beloved of Allah). A true lover must be patient with trials from the Beloved. Thus 'Sabur' is appropriate from his own name.
The effect of a name on its bearer is a recognized idea.
4
Analyze the teacher's anecdote
Reflect on the teacher's remark that the author 'made his own father his slave' by attributing a divine name to himself by inheritance. This highlights sensitivity in using divine attributes for humans.
It shows scholarly awareness of proper attribution.
5
Examine the opening supplication
The author prays 'May Allah make him reach the peak of perfection'. Analyze the words 'dhirwah' (peak) and 'kamal' (perfection). Note that perfection is defined as firm belief and righteous deeds.
This sets the goal for the study of usul al-fiqh.

یعنی وصف اول ( شکور ) کا ذکر بر بنائے ارث ہے چنانچہ ہر نام کے آدمی پر اس کے نام کے اچھے برے نتائج مرتب ہوئے ہیں اگر نام اسماء الہیہ کی طرف منسوب یا اسماء النبی میں سے کوئی ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس نام پاک کے برکات و اثرات صاحب نام شخص پر مرتب ہوں گے چونکہ مصنف کے والد محترم کا نام نامی عبدالشکور ہے اور نام کا اثر ہوتا ہے تو معنی شکور کا کچھ نصیب و حصہ یا برکات ان کے والد کے لئے ہوں گے۔ اور لڑکا الولد سر لابیہ کے مطابق ظاہر و باطن میں بالیکا جانشین ووارث ہوتا ہے پس اسم شکور کے برکات ان کے والد عبدالشکور میں تھے وہ بر بنائے وراثت مصنف میں منتقل ہوئے تو مصنف بھی شکور ہوئے ۔ اس لئے کہا الوصف الاول كانه بالارث صبور جو دوسری صفت ہے اس کو اپنے نام کی مناسبت سے ذکر کیا ہے ابھی گذرا کہ آدمی کی ذات پر اس کے نام کا اثر ہوتا ہے پس جس طرح مصنف کے والد پر ان کے نام عبد الشکور کا اثر مرتب ہوا ایسی ہی مصنف پر بھی ان کے نام محب اللہ کا اثر ظاہر ہے چونکہ جب مصنف کا نام محب اللہ ہے تو محب کی حالت کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ مالک ارض و سماء کی طرف سے نازل ہونے والے بلاء ومصیبت پر صبر کرے کہ محبت حقیقی دی ہے جو بوقت مصیبت زبان پر حرف شکایت نہ لائے گویا مصنف کا نام ہی دال ہے مصنف کے صابر ہونے پر اس لئے مصنف نے الشکور الصبور کہا۔ لطیفہ۔ مسلم الثبوت کی ایک شرح قلمی جو ۲۵ شعبان ۱۱۸۰ھ کی تصنیف ہے اس کتاب میں متن کی عبارت " اما بعد فيقول الشكور الصبور محب الله بن عبدالشكور“ کی شرح کرتے ہوئے لکھا فی الحاشية الوصف الاول كــانــه بالارث والوصف الثـانـي كـانـه بنفسہ اس کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ طلبہ میں یہ بات مشہور ہے کہ مصنف نے اس کتاب کو تصنیف کرنے کے بعد اپنے استاذ عالم تحریر، ذکی خبیر شیخ قطب الدین شمس آبادی کی خدمت میں بھیجا انہوں نے جب یہ عبارت دیکھی تو فرمایا کہ یہ اس نے کیا کیا ؟ کہ اپنے باب کو اپنا غلام بنالیا۔ شکور ثانی اسمائے الہیہ میں سے ہے جیسا کہ ان اللہ غفور شکور میں ارشاد ہے معنی ہے شکر پر بدلہ عطا فرمانے والا ، کہ جزائے شکر کو بھی شکر سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں جیسے کہ قرآن میں جزائے سیدہ کو سینہ سے تعبیر فرمایا گیا ارشاد ہے جزاء سيئة سيئة مثلها ۔ یہ بھی قول ہے کہ شکور طاعت قلیل پر خیر کثیر عطا کرنے والے کو کہتے ہیں اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالی چند دنوں کی مختصری طاعت پر جنت جیسی دائی دسرمدی نعمت عطا فرمائے گا۔ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ شکور وہ جو اپنے اطاعت گزار کی طاعت پر اس کی تعریف کرنے والا ہو۔ قوله - بلغه الله الى ذروة الكمال الخ اس کا قول بلغہ تشدیدلام کے ساتھ تبلیغ کا ماضی بمنزلہ انشاء ایصال کے معنی میں ہے۔ ذروة ضمہ وکسرہ دونوں کے ساتھ آیا ہے ہر چیز کی بلندی خصوصاً پہاڑ کے بالائی حصہ چوٹی کو کہتے ہیں ، بطور استعارہ مراتب عالیہ مراد ہے۔ یا کہ کمال کو جبل سے تشبیہ دی ہے مگر مشبہ بہ جبل کو جذف کر کے اس کے لئے ذروہ کو بطور استعارہ بالکنا یہ انتخیلیہ کے ذکر کیا ہے اور کمال تمام کو کہتے ہیں جیسا کہ قاموس میں ہے اس سے مراد، اعمال صالحہ ، صفات حسنہ اور نفوس زا کیہ کا وہ منتھی ہے جہاں تک عروج انسان کی انتہا ممکن ہے۔ حفیض، پستی زمین در دامن کوہ کے معنی میں آتا ہے، ایک نسخہ میں بالصاد ٹھملہ قرار ارض کے معنی میں آیا ہے۔ قال وقیل یہ دونوں اسم میں قول کے معنی میں ، کہا جاتا ہے کثــر الــقـيــل والقال ، حدیث شریف میں ہے نھی عن قیل وقال ، فارسی میں بڑا مشہور شعر ہے خوشا مسجد و مدرسه و خانقاه که در وے بود قیل و قال محمد یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے خیر کیلئے قیل اور شر کے لئے قال کا استعمال ہوتا ہے قلة الحال ضمہ کے ساتھ پہاڑ کی چوٹی اور ہر چیز کی بلندی کو کہتے ہیں حال اس درجہ کو کہتے ہیں جس پر بچہ چڑھتا ہے جب چلنے لگتا ہے لیکن بطور استعارہ درجات عالیہ اور مرتبہ رفیعہ مراد ہے۔ قوله ان السعادة باستكمال النفس والمادة الخ اس کے قول السعادة پر ال عوض کا ہے سعادۃ الانسان تقدیر عبارت ہوگی ، یا پھر ال عہد کا ہے یعنی سعادت مخصوصہ جود نیاوی وآخروی سعادت ہے ، شقاوت کی ضد ہے تحقق ، سے عقائد کی پختگی اور تخلق ، سے اعمال صالحہ سے آراستگی مراد ہے جبکہ نفس، روح اور مادہ جسم کے معنی میں ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان اس وقت تک درجہ کمال کو نہیں پہونچ سکتا ہے جب تک کہ انسان عقائد دینیہ کے معلومات میں راسخ اور اعمال صالحہ
That is, the first attribute (Shakur) is mentioned on the basis of inheritance. Thus, for every name, good and bad consequences are attached to the person bearing it. If the name is derived from the divine names or from the names of the Prophet, it is obvious that the blessings and effects of that pure name will be attached to the person bearing it. Since the author's respected father's name is 'Abd al-Shakur, and the name has an effect, some portion or blessings of the meaning of Shakur will be for his father. And the son, according to 'al-waladu sirru abihi' (the son is the secret of his father), is the successor and heir in appearance and inner reality. Thus the blessings of the name Shakur were in his father 'Abd al-Shakur; they transferred to the author by way of inheritance, so the author also became Shakur. Therefore, he said: the first attribute is as if by inheritance. Sabur, the second attribute, is mentioned due to the appropriateness of his own name. It has already passed that a person's name has an effect on his being. Just as the effect of the name 'Abd al-Shakur occurred on the author's father, similarly the effect of the name 'Muhibb Allah' is apparent on the author. Since the author's name is Muhibb Allah, the state of a lover requires that he be patient with the calamities and afflictions sent by the Lord of the heavens and the earth, because real love is that which does not bring a word of complaint upon the tongue at the time of affliction. Thus the author's very name indicates his being patient. Therefore the author said 'al-Shakur al-Sabur'. Anecdote: In a manuscript commentary of Muslim al-Thubut, authored on 25 Sha'ban 1180 AH, while explaining the text's phrase 'Amma ba'd, fa-yaqulu al-Shakur al-Sabur Muhibb Allah ibn 'Abd al-Shakur', it is written in the margin: 'The first attribute is as if by inheritance, and the second attribute is as if from himself'. After that, it is written that it is famous among students that when the author finished compiling this book, he sent it to his teacher, the learned, eloquent, intelligent, and perceptive Shaykh Qutb al-Din Shamsabadi. When he saw this phrase, he said: 'What has he done? He has made his own father his slave.' Shakur is among the divine names, as in the verse 'Inna Allaha Ghafur Shakur' (Indeed Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Appreciative). Its meaning is: One who rewards for gratitude (shukr). Indeed, the reward for gratitude is also expressed by the word shukr, just as in the Quran the reward for an evil deed is expressed by the word sayyi'ah, as in the verse 'Jaza'u sayyi'atin sayyi'atum mithluha' (The recompense of an evil deed is an evil deed like it). It is also said that Shakur is the One who gives abundant good for little obedience, because Allah will give an eternal blessing like Paradise for the brief obedience of a few days. It is also said that Shakur is the One who praises His obedient servant for his obedience. His saying 'ballaghahu Allahu ila dhirwati al-kamal' (May Allah make him reach the peak of perfection) — his saying 'ballaghahu' with tashdid on the lam is the past tense of tabligh, in the sense of isal (causing to reach), used as a prayer. 'Dhirwah' appears with damma and kasra (dhirwah and dhirwah) — it means the height of everything, especially the top of a mountain, and metaphorically, high ranks. Or it is said that perfection (kamal) is likened to a mountain, but the object of comparison (the mountain) is omitted, and its peak (dhirwah) is mentioned as a creative metaphorical reference. And 'kamal' is said to mean completeness, as in the Qamus. By it is meant the ultimate of righteous deeds, good qualities, and pure souls to the extent possible for human ascension. 'Hafid' means low ground at the foot of a mountain. In one copy it is written with 'sad' (hasf?) meaning 'ground'. 'Qal wa qil' both are nouns meaning 'speech'. It is said: 'Kathura al-qilu wa al-qalu' (Such sayings abound). The noble hadith states: 'He forbade qil and qal.' In Persian there is a famous verse: 'How good the mosque and school and monastery, in which is qil and qal of Muhammad.' It is also said that 'qil' is used for good and 'qal' for evil. 'Qillat al-hal' with damma means the peak of a mountain and the height of everything. 'Hal' is the level a child climbs when he begins to walk, but metaphorically, high ranks and lofty stations are meant. His saying 'inna al-sa'adata bi-istikmali al-nafsi wa al-maddah' (Indeed happiness [lies] in perfecting the soul and the matter) — his saying 'al-sa'adah' the 'al' is for substitution, so the premise is 'sa'adat al-insan' (the happiness of a human), or the 'al' is for precedence, i.e., the specific happiness which is the happiness of this world and the Hereafter, the opposite of wretchedness. 'Tahaqquq' means firmness of beliefs, and 'takhalluq' means adornment with righteous deeds. 'Nafs' means spirit, and 'maddah' means body. The meaning is that a person cannot reach the level of perfection until he is firmly grounded in the knowledge of religious beliefs and [adorned with] righteous deeds.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is from the opening of the sharh (commentary) on Muslim al-Thubut, explaining the author's self-description and opening prayer. The author, Muhibb Allah ibn 'Abd al-Shakur, calls himself 'al-Shakur al-Sabur'. The commentator explains that 'Shakur' is attributed to the author by way of inheritance from his father, 'Abd al-Shakur, because a name's effects transfer to offspring. 'Sabur' is attributed to his own name 'Muhibb Allah', as a lover must be patient. An anecdote relates that the author's teacher remarked that the author made his own father his slave by attributing the divine attribute 'Shakur' to himself by inheritance. Then the meaning of 'Shakur' as a divine attribute is discussed: the One who rewards gratitude, or gives much for little, or praises the obedient. Then the supplication 'May Allah cause him to reach the peak of perfection' is linguistically analyzed: 'dhirwah' is peak, 'kamal' is completeness. Finally, the statement 'Happiness lies in perfecting the soul and the matter' is clarified: perfection requires firm belief and righteous deeds. This passage is introductory and not directly usul al-fiqh, but it sets the stage for the author's approach.

Key Terms
شکور (Shakur): A divine attribute meaning the One who rewards abundantly for little obedience, or praises the obedient servant.
صبور (Sabur): Patient; the author applies it to himself because his name Muhibb Allah requires patience in affliction.
ذروة (dhirwah): Peak or summit, used metaphorically for the highest rank.
كمال (kamal): Completeness, perfection, the ultimate level of righteous deeds and good qualities.
سعادة (sa'adah): Happiness, both worldly and otherworldly, achieved by perfecting the soul and body through firm belief and righteous deeds.
الولد سر لابيه (al-waladu sirru abihi): The son is the secret of his father; meaning the son inherits inner qualities from his father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author describe himself as 'al-Shakur'?
A) Because he was very grateful to Allah.
B) Because his father's name was 'Abd al-Shakur and he inherited the attribute.
C) Because his teacher commanded him to use that title.
D) Because he wanted to imitate the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi tradition, a scholar's self-description can be rooted in spiritual lineage and the effects of names, reflecting a deep connection between personal identity and divine attributes.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Virtue and Status of Usul al-Fiqh
Commentary on the praise of usul al-fiqh and clarification of its rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul al-fiqh is regarded as a great science in a relative sense, and distinguish its foundational role from absolute superiority over other Islamic sciences like tawhid.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is great not absolutely, but as a foundational science — like 'ilm al-tawhid.

This passage from the commentary on Musallam al-Thubot praises usul al-fiqh as among the greatest Islamic sciences. However, the commentator immediately clarifies that this praise does not mean usul is superior to the science of tawhid. Instead, its greatness is relative: it is foundational for fiqh, just as kalam is foundational for beliefs. Understanding this distinction prevents a common misunderstanding and sets the proper hierarchy of Islamic learning.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the praise language
Identify phrases like 'ajal al-'ulum' (greatest sciences) and 'khutab fi madhihi' (sermons in its praise). Note the commentator's caution that this is praise (madḥ), not a claim of absolute superiority.
The author uses rhetorical exaggeration common in introductions.
2
Distinguish relative vs. absolute greatness
The commentator introduces the concept of 'jalāla iḍāfiyya' (relative grandeur). Usul is great because it is a principle (mabda') for fiqh, just as kalam is a principle for usul. It is not greater than the science of tawhid in an absolute sense.
This prevents the erroneous notion that usul outranks tawhid.
3
Understand the interdependence of sciences
The passage explains that true happiness (sa'āda) requires firm belief and righteous deeds. Righteous deeds are guided by fiqh, and fiqh depends on usul. Usul itself depends on kalam (theology). Thus, usul is a necessary, but not ultimate, science.
The chain: Kalam → Usul al-Fiqh → Fiqh → Righteous deeds → Happiness.
4
Analyze the author's claim of mastery
The author claims to have probed the deepest secrets (daqā’iq) of usul. This is an expression of gratitude for divine favor (taḥdīth al-ni‘ma), not arrogance. It shows the high level of mastery required in this science.
Such claims are customary in scholarly prefaces.

عطا کرنے والے کو کہتے ہیں اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ چند دنوں کی مختصری طاعت پر جنت جیسی دائمی سرمدی نعمت عطا فرمائے گا۔ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ شکور وہ جو اپنے اطاعت گزار کی طاعت پر اس کی تعریف کرنے والا ہو۔

حفیض، پستی زمین در دامن کوہ کے معنی میں آتا ہے، ایک نسخہ میں بالصاد ٹھملہ قرار ارض کے معنی میں آیا ہے۔ قال وقیل یہ دونوں اسم میں قول کے معنی میں ، کہا جاتا ہے کثر القیل والقال ، حدیث شریف میں ہے نہی عن قیل وقال ، فارسی میں بڑا مشہور شعر ہے خوشا مسجد و مدرسه و خانقاه که در وے بود قیل و قال محمد۔ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے خیر کیلئے قیل اور شر کے لئے قال کا استعمال ہوتا ہے قلعة الحال ضمہ کے ساتھ پہاڑ کی چوٹی اور ہر چیز کی بلندی کو کہتے ہیں حال اس درجہ کو کہتے ہیں جس پر بچہ چڑھتا ہے جب چلنے لگتا ہے لیکن بطور استعارہ درجات عالیہ اور مرتبہ رفیعہ مراد ہے۔

قوله : " فهومن اجل علوم الاسلام الف في مدحه خطب " الخ مطلب یہ ہے علم اصول فقہ علم کلام و عقائد حقہ (جو مبدا و معاد اور ذات وصفات باری تعالیٰ سے متعلق ہیں ) کی معرفت کے بعد اجل علوم اسلامیہ ہے مصنف کی عبارت کا یہ مطلب ہر گز نہیں ہے کہ جملہ علوم اسلامیہ سے یہ افضل واجل علم ہے یہاں تک کہ اعتراض واقع ہو کہ یہ علم علم توحید سے کیونکر افضل ہو سکتا ہے؟ غرض اصول فقہ کو جو اصل و افضل کہا گیا ہے اس سے جلالت حقیقیہ نہیں مراد ہے بلکہ جلالت اضافیہ مراد ہے کہ جس طرح علم توحید وصفات اجل علوم میں سے ہے کہ وہ مبادی میں سے ہے ایسے ہی علم اصول بھی مبادی میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے اجل علوم کہلانے کا مستحق ہے۔ یا یہ کہا جائے کہ مصنف کا یہ کلام مدح پر مبنی ہے جیسا کہ تمام مصنفین کا طریقہ ہے۔ اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ علم اصول تمامی علوم میں فی الواقع بھی اجل واشرف ہے ... اس کا قول خُطب خطبہ کی جمع ہے کہا جاتا ہے خطب على المبنز خطبہ کلام منثور مجمع کو خطبہ کہتے ہیں۔ قواعد قاعدہ کی جمع ہے وہ قضیہ کلیہ جس پر جزئیات منطبق ہوتے ہیں قاعدہ کہلاتا ہے۔
قوله ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق ماربه الخ، مارب بالمد جمع ہے مارب کی ۔ ارب " سے ماخوذ ہے مطلب و مقصد کے معنی میں ہے حقیقہ ، سے فن کے قواعد و مسائل مراد ہیں اس لئے کہ فن کی حقیقت اس کے مسائل ہوتے ہیں اور دقیقہ سے فن کے رموز و اسرار اور نکات و لطائف مراد ہیں۔ معنی یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے فن اصول فقہ کو اس گہرائی نظر سے مطالعہ کیا کہ فن کے قواعد و مسائل تو کیا اس کے نکات و لطائف اور رموز و اسرار سے بھی واقف ہو گئے حتی کہ ان سے اس فن کا کوئی درمکنون پوشیدہ نہ رہ سکا، مصنف نے اس مقام پر اپنی صلاحیت و ہمہ دانی کا اظہار تحدیث نعمت کے طور پر کیا ہے جیسا کہ مصلحین کا یہ طریقہ رہا ہے خصوصاً
A giver is called one who gives, because Allah will give an eternal blessing like Paradise for a few days of brief obedience. It is also said that Shakur is one who praises his obedient servant for his obedience. His saying 'May Allah bring him to the peak of perfection' etc.: the word 'ballaghahu' with tashdid on lam is the past tense of 'tabligh' in the sense of conveying, used as an inceptive. 'Dhirwa' comes with dammah and kasrah; it means the height of everything, especially the upper part of a mountain, the peak; metaphorically, high ranks are intended. Or it is said that perfection is likened to a mountain, but the mountain as the object of comparison is omitted and 'dhirwa' is mentioned as a metaphorical allusion by way of representation. And 'kamal' means completeness, as in the dictionary; what is intended is the end of righteous deeds, good attributes, and purified souls, to the extent that human ascent is possible. 'Hafid' means low ground at the foot of a mountain; in one copy with 'sad' it appears in the sense of low ground. 'Qal wa qil' are both nouns in the sense of speech. It is said 'Kathir al-qil wa al-qal', and in the hadith it is forbidden from qil and qal. In Persian there is a famous verse: 'How delightful is the mosque, school, and monastery where there is qil and qal of Muhammad.' It is also said that 'qil' is used for good and 'qal' for evil. 'Qilat al-hal' with dammah means the peak of a mountain and the height of everything; 'hal' means the stage that a child climbs when he begins to walk, but metaphorically high degrees and lofty stations are intended. His saying 'Indeed happiness is through perfecting the soul and matter' etc.: the 'al' on 'sa'ada' is of compensation; the phrase would be 'sa'adat al-insan' in estimate, or it is 'al' of covenant, i.e., specific happiness which is worldly and otherworldly happiness, opposite of misery. 'Tahqiuq' refers to firmness of beliefs, and 'takhalluq' refers to adornment with righteous deeds. 'Nafs' means spirit, and 'madda' means body. The meaning is that man cannot reach the degree of perfection until he is firm in the knowledge of religious beliefs and adorned with righteous deeds, because eternal happiness is attained only after traversing the stages of faith and works. Then their attainment is possible only after gaining depth in fiqh and firmness and perfection in the path of truth and certainty, i.e., in beliefs. And the attainment of depth in religion depends on the attainment of the principles of fiqh; therefore, before fiqh, it is necessary to attain the principles of fiqh, such as kalam and usul al-fiqh. His saying 'So it is among the greatest sciences of Islam; so many sermons were composed in its praise' etc.: The meaning is that the science of usul al-fiqh, after the knowledge of kalam and true beliefs (which pertain to the beginning and end and the essence and attributes of Allah Almighty), is among the greatest Islamic sciences. The author's phrase does not mean that it is the greatest and noblest of all Islamic sciences, to the extent that objection would arise that how can this science be greater than the science of tawhid? In short, when usul al-fiqh is called original and superior, what is intended is not real grandeur but relative grandeur; just as the science of tawhid and attributes is among the greatest sciences because it is among the principles, similarly the science of usul is also worthy of being called the greatest because it is among the principles. Or it may be said that the author's statement is based on praise, as is the way of all authors; this does not imply that the science of usul is actually the greatest and most noble among all sciences. His saying 'khutab' is the plural of 'khutbah'; it is said 'khataba 'ala al-minbari'; khutbah is a prose speech addressed to a gathering. 'Qawa'id' is the plural of 'qa'idah'; it is called a universal proposition to which particulars conform. His saying 'And I entrusted my sight to achieving its goals etc.': 'Marib' with madd is the plural of 'marib', derived from 'arab' in the sense of need and purpose. 'Tahqiq' refers to the rules and issues of the art, because the reality of the art is its issues. 'Daqiqah' refers to the secrets and mysteries of the art and its subtleties and fine points. The meaning is that the author studied the art of usul al-fiqh with such depth of insight that he became acquainted not only with its rules and issues but also with its subtleties and secrets, so much so that no hidden gem of this art remained concealed from him. The author displayed his ability and comprehensiveness at this point as a gratitude for the blessing, as is the way of reformers, especially.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary of Ashraf al-Nu'ut on Musallam al-Thubut. It begins by explaining the meaning of 'Shakur' (the Grateful) as an attribute of Allah, indicating that He grants eternal paradise for brief obedience. The commentator then explicates the author's phrase 'May Allah bring him to the peak of perfection,' breaking down the linguistic and metaphorical aspects of the words 'dhirwa' (peak) and 'kamal' (perfection), showing that perfection encompasses righteous actions, good qualities, and purified souls. The distinction between 'qil' and 'qal' is clarified—'qil' is for good talk, 'qal' for evil. The commentary on 'sa'ada' (happiness) links worldly and otherworldly happiness to firm beliefs and righteous deeds, arguing that true perfection comes only after mastering the principles of fiqh, which necessitate prior study of kalam and usul al-fiqh. Crucially, the commentator stresses that usul al-fiqh is among the greatest sciences not absolutely but relatively—it is great as a foundational science, just as 'ilm al-tawhid is great; this prevents the misinterpretation that it surpasses tawhid. The final part praises the author's deep insight into the art, having mastered its rules and hidden secrets. The commentary is expository, clarifying terms and preventing misinterpretation.

Key Terms
ذروة (dhirwa): The peak or highest point of a mountain; metaphorically, the highest rank or station.
حفیض (hafīḍ): Low ground at the foot of a mountain; also used for the opposite of 'dhirwa'.
سعادة (sa'āda): Happiness that encompasses both worldly and otherworldly perfection, attained through firm belief and righteous deeds.
قیل وقال (qīl wa qāl): Idle talk or gossip; 'qīl' is for good speech and 'qāl' for evil speech as per the explanation.
جلالة إضافية (jalāla iḍāfiyya): Relative grandeur – greatness in relation to something else, not absolute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is usul al-fiqh called 'among the greatest sciences' (ajal al-'ulum) without implying absolute superiority?
A) Because it is the most important science in Islam.
B) Because it is a foundational (mabadi') science like 'ilm al-tawhid, so its greatness is relative.
C) Because it is superior to all other sciences including tawhid.
D) Because the author was simply exaggerating in praise.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is a foundational science; its greatness is relative, not absolute, and it complements rather than supersedes ‘ilm al-tawhid.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Why Usul al-Fiqh is a Prerequisite for Fiqh
Argues for the necessity of usul al-fiqh as a prerequisite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why usul al-fiqh is a necessary preliminary science (mabadi) for fiqh according to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is a prerequisite for fiqh; without it, true tafaqquh is impossible.

This passage, from a commentary on a Hanafi usul text, establishes the indispensability of usul al-fiqh as a foundational science. It argues that genuine understanding of religion (tafaqquh fi al-din) cannot be achieved without first mastering the principles (mabadi) that underpin fiqh. The author specifically mentions two such principles: kalam (theology) and usul al-fiqh itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ultimate goal
The passage begins by stating that eternal happiness (sa'adat) is attained only after traversing the stages of faith (iman) and action (amal). Recognise that the ultimate aim is to reach this state through correct belief and practice.
2
Identify the means to the goal
The passage then states that this happiness requires expertise in fiqh and firmness in beliefs (i'tiqadiyat). Note that both legal knowledge and sound theology are essential.
3
Identify the prerequisites for those means
It then asserts that 'tafaqquh fi al-din' (deep understanding of religion) depends on the acquisition of the 'mabadi al-fiqh' (principles of fiqh). This is the key move: fiqh itself cannot be properly understood without its foundational sciences.
4
List the mabadi
The passage explicitly identifies kalam and usul al-fiqh as the two required preliminary sciences. Understand that 'kalam' provides correct beliefs, while 'usul al-fiqh' provides the methodology for deriving rulings.
5
Derive the order of study
Since tafaqquh depends on mabadi, and mabadi include usul al-fiqh, it logically follows that one must study usul al-fiqh before fiqh. This is the central thesis: usul al-fiqh is not optional but a necessary preliminary science.
The passage uses the word 'لازم' (necessary) to stress obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے آراستہ نہ ہو جائے کیونکہ ایمان و عمل کے مدارج طے کرنے کے بعد ہی سعادت سرمدی حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ پھر ان دونوں کا حصول فقہ میں تجر حاصل کرنے اور راہ حق و یقین یعنی اعتقادیات میں پختگی اور کمال حاصل کرنے کے بعد ہی ممکن ہے اور تفقہ فی الدین کا حصول مبادی فقہ کے حصول پر موقوف ہے لہذ ا فقہ کے پہلے، مبادی فقہ مثلاً کلام و اصول فقہ کا حصول لازم ہے۔
It is not adorned until after traversing the stages of faith and action, eternal happiness is attained. Then the acquisition of both is possible only after obtaining expertise in fiqh and firmness and perfection in the path of truth and certainty, i.e., beliefs. And the acquisition of understanding in religion (tafaqquh fi al-din) depends on acquiring the principles of fiqh. Therefore, before fiqh, it is necessary to acquire the principles of fiqh, such as kalam and usul al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the necessity of studying usul al-fiqh. It argues that true happiness (sa'adat) is achieved only after perfecting both faith (iman) and action (amal). Mastery in fiqh and certainty in beliefs (i'tiqadiyat) must be attained first. Since understanding religion (tafaqquh) depends on the principles (mabadi) of fiqh, one must first learn the foundational sciences: kalam (theology) and usul al-fiqh. The author emphasizes that usul al-fiqh is a prerequisite for fiqh, establishing its importance as a preliminary science.

Key Terms
مبادی فقہ (mabadi al-fiqh): The foundational sciences that are prerequisites for fiqh, such as kalam and usul al-fiqh.
تفقہ فی الدین (tafaqquh fi al-din): Deep understanding of religion, particularly in matters of fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only kalam
B) Only usul al-fiqh
C) Both kalam and usul al-fiqh
D) Only beliefs

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is a compulsory preliminary science (mabadi) for any serious student of fiqh.

The Scholar's Humility in Claiming Mastery: Tahdith al-Ni'mah
Explains the author's claim of thorough investigation into the subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meanings of haqiqah and daqiqah in the context of usul al-fiqh and identify the concept of tahdith al-ni'mah as expressed by scholars.

Core Idea
A scholar's claim of mastery is gratitude, not pride — tahdith al-ni'mah justifies self-praise.

This passage from a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut reveals how classical scholars framed their intellectual achievements. The author claims to have studied usul al-fiqh so deeply that he mastered both its explicit rules and its hidden subtleties. But this is not arrogance; it is a form of thanking Allah for blessing him with knowledge, known as tahdith al-ni'mah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
Locate the phrase 'ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق ماربه' and understand that the author is asserting thorough investigation of the discipline's goals.
This is a common trope in scholarly introductions, not a boast.
2
Parse the key terms
Extract the definitions of marib, haqiqah, and daqiqah from the commentary. Marib = goals; haqiqah = rules and issues; daqiqah = subtle points and secrets.
These terms distinguish between surface knowledge and deep mastery.
3
Understand the purpose: tahdith al-ni'mah
Recognize that the author's expression of mastery is actually an act of gratitude, as the commentator explicitly notes. This is a standard scholarly practice to acknowledge divine favor.
Tahdith al-ni'mah is rooted in Quranic injunctions to speak of blessings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق ماربه الخ، مارب بالمد جمع ہے مارب کی ۔ ارب " سے ماخوذ ہے مطلب و مقصد کے معنی میں ہے حقیقہ ، سے فن کے قواعد و مسائل مراد ہیں اس لئے کہ فن کی حقیقت اس کے مسائل ہوتے ہیں اور دقیقہ سے فن کے رموز و اسرار اور نکات و لطائف مراد ہیں۔ معنی یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے فن اصول فقہ کو اس گہرائی نظر سے مطالعہ کیا کہ فن کے قواعد و مسائل تو کیا اس کے نکات و لطائف اور رموز و اسرار سے بھی واقف ہو گئے حتی کہ ان سے اس فن کا کوئی در مکنون پوشیدہ نہ رہ سکا، مصنف نے اس مقام پر اپنی صلاحیت و ہمہ دانی کا اظہار تحدیث نعمت کے طور پر کیا ہے جیسا کہ مصلحین کا یہ طریقہ رہا ہے خصوصاً
His statement: 'And I turned my attention to investigating its goals' etc. 'Marib' (with lengthening) is plural of 'maribah', derived from 'arb', meaning aim and objective. 'Haqiqah' refers to the rules and issues of the discipline, because the reality of a discipline is its issues. 'Daqiqah' refers to the subtleties and secrets, fine points and witticisms of the discipline. The meaning is that the author studied the discipline of usul al-fiqh with such penetrating vision that he became acquainted not only with its rules and issues but also with its subtleties, secrets, and fine points, so much so that no hidden depth of this discipline remained concealed from him. The author here expresses his own capability and comprehensiveness as a form of expressing gratitude for blessings, as is the way of reformers, especially...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage comments on the author's phrase 'ووكلت نظرى الى تحقيق ماربه' (I turned my attention to investigating its goals). The commentator explains 'marib' as goals or objectives, 'haqiqah' as the actual rules and issues of the discipline, and 'daqiqah' as the subtle points and secrets. The author claims to have studied usul al-fiqh so deeply that he mastered both its explicit rules and its hidden subtleties. This expression of mastery is not arrogance but a form of gratitude (tahdith al-ni'mah) for the knowledge bestowed upon him, as is customary among scholars.

Key Terms
مارب (marib): Plural of maribah, meaning aims, goals, or purposes.
حقیقہ (haqiqah): The essence of a discipline, comprising its rules and issues (masa'il).
دقیقہ (daqiqah): Subtle points, secrets, and fine details of a discipline.
تحدیث نعمت (tahdith al-ni'mah): Expressing gratitude for blessings by acknowledging them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To prove his superiority over other scholars
B) To express gratitude for Allah's blessing
C) To encourage students to study harder
D) To establish the importance of usul al-fiqh

Key Takeaway
A scholar's declaration of mastery in usul al-fiqh is ethically framed as tahdith al-ni'mah, not arrogance.

The Final Cause of Scholarship: Intent in Authoring a Book of Usul
Author's purpose and final cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the concept of 'illah gha'iyyah (final cause) in the context of authoring a scholarly usul work and explain why multiple noble purposes are permissible.

Core Idea
A scholar's intent in compiling a book can be any noble aim, not limited to one specific goal.

As we begin studying a classical usul al-fiqh text, understanding the author's motivation is essential. This passage from the commentary reveals that the author's purpose is not singular; rather, several noble objectives are possible—seeking divine pleasure, guiding students, or even earning the ruler's favor. This teaches us that scholarly work can serve multiple legitimate ends, as long as the core intention remains sincere.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase
Locate the phrase 'li-amr' in the Arabic text and note the tanwin al-ta'dhim (نون تعظیم). This grammatical feature indicates greatness.
Tanwin on indefinite nouns often conveys exaltation or generality.
2
Understand 'illah gha'iyyah'
Recognize that 'illah gha'iyyah means 'final cause'—the purpose for which an act is done. Here, the author's act of writing the book has a final cause.
In usul al-fiqh, 'illah gha'iyyah is used to discuss the objectives of Islamic law (maqasid).
3
List the possible purposes
From the commentary, extract the list of possible purposes: seeking proximity to the ruler, impressing scholars, guiding students, or attaining happiness in both worlds.
The commentator does not rank these; all are valid.
4
Connect to broader usul principle
Relate this to the concept that intentions (niyyah) affect the validity and reward of actions. In fiqh, acts are judged by intentions (al-umur bi-maqasidiha).
This principle is universal, but here applied to authorship.
5
Reflect on scholarly motivation
Consider why a scholar might mention such purposes. It encourages students to purify their intentions and recognize the high stakes of producing ilm.
This reflection bridges the author's time to our contemporary context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ثم لامرما اردت أن احرر سفراً وافياً الخ، اس کا قول لامر میں تنوین تعظیم کی ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ ایک عظیم مقصد اس کتاب کی تصنیف کی علت غائیہ ہے امر عظیم مصنف کے نزدیک خواہ سلطان عصر کا تقرب ہو خواہ اپنے معاصر علماء پر اپنی علمی دھاگ اور ذہانت کا سکہ بٹھانا ہو چاہے اس فن کے طلبہ کو حق وصواب کی راہ دکھانا ہو یا سعادت دارین کا حصول مقصود ہو اور یہ علماء دین سے زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ سفر اگرہ کے ساتھ جمع اس کی اسفار آتی ہے دفتر ی عظیم و نیم کتاب کے معنی میں بولا جاتا ہے قرآن حکیم میں ہے کمثل الحمار تجمل اسفاراً۔
His statement: 'Then, for a great purpose, I wished to compile a comprehensive volume' etc. In his expression 'for a purpose' (li-amr), the tanwin indicates greatness. The meaning is that a great objective is the final cause for authoring this book. The great purpose could be: seeking proximity to the ruler of the time, or impressing contemporary scholars with his intellectual prowess and genius, or guiding students of this discipline to the path of truth and correctness, or attaining happiness in both worlds. This is more apparent to religious scholars. 'Safar' (volume) has the plural 'asfar', and is used to mean a great book or a tome. In the Holy Quran it is said: 'Like the donkey carrying volumes' (62:5).
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage comments on the author's phrase 'ثم لامرما اردت أن احرر سفراً وافياً' (Then, for a great purpose, I wished to compile a comprehensive volume). The commentator explains that the tanwin on 'amr' indicates greatness, so 'a great purpose' is the final cause ('illah gha'iyyah) of the book. This purpose could be any noble aim: seeking favor from the ruler, displaying scholarly acumen, guiding students, or attaining eternal happiness. The commentator also notes that 'safar' means a large book, citing the Quranic verse 'like the donkey carrying volumes'.

Key Terms
علت غائیہ ('illah gha'iyyah): The final cause or purpose for which an act is done.
سفر (safar): A large book or volume, often a comprehensive work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The purpose is great
C) The purpose is small
D) There is no purpose

Key Takeaway
A scholarly work can be motivated by multiple noble purposes, and recognizing this enriches our appreciation of the author's intent.

The Book's Commitment to Objective Presentation of Madhhab Views
Explains that the book presents both Hanafi and Shafi'i views fairly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological principle of objectivity in presenting conflicting madhhab positions as exemplified by the author of Musallam al-Thubut.

Core Idea
This book presents both Hanafi and Shafi'i views exactly as they are, without distortion – truth-seeking, not blind partisanship.

In this passage, the commentator explains that the author of the matn (Musallam al-Thubut) deliberately avoids sectarian bias. He reports each school's position faithfully, even when it conflicts with his own. This reflects a core principle of classical Hanafi usul: the pursuit of truth (tahqiq al-haqq) over mere taqlid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn phrase being expanded
Locate the phrase 'ولايميل ميلاما عن الواقعية' in the passage and note it as the starting point of the commentary.
This phrase is the key to understanding the commentator's intent.
2
Analyze the first interpretation (reporting exactly without distortion)
The commentator says the book reports statements from both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools 'بعينه من و عن' (exactly as they are), without twisting or altering.
Emphasize the phrase 'بعينہ من و عن'.
3
Analyze the second interpretation (striving for truth as per human capability)
The commentator adds that the book aims to mention statements based on truth as far as humanly possible, but notes that absolute truth with Allah is beyond reach.
Distinguish between human effort and divine knowledge.
4
Recognize the limitation and contrast with blind imitation
The book does not claim infallibility; it is free from sectarian bias, unlike books of 'mere blind followers' who imitate ancestors without verification.
The final sentence contrasts the book's approach with taqlid.
5
Summarize the book's methodological stance
Combine the above points: objective reporting, truth-seeking, and refutation of falsehood, all without distortion or bias.
This methodological stance is a hallmark of rigorous usul scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله - ولايميل ميلاما عن الواقعية الخ ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ کتاب «مسلم ، حنفی و شافعی مسلک میں وضع کردہ مسائل کے ذکر پر مبنی ہے جن کا جو مذہب ہے بعینہ من و عن ان کے اقوال کو بیان کیا گیا ہے کسی بھی مذہب کو توڑ مروڑ کر یا اس میں تغیر وتصرف بھیجا کر کے خلاف واقعہ نہیں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ یا یہ معنی ہے کہ طاقت بشریہ کے مطابق حتی الامکان حقائق پر مبنی اقوال ذکر کئے گئے ہیں۔ یہ معنی نہیں ہے کہ جو عند اللہ حق ہے دھی مذکور ہے اس لئے کہ یہ صرف اور صرف اللہ خالق قوم علیم وخبیر عالم الغیب والشھادۃ کی شان ہے ہاں اسکی عطاء سے اس کے خلفاء ارضین انبیاء مرسلین اور اولیاء کاملین جان سکتے ہیں۔ اس میں اشارہ ہے کہ یہ کتاب حقانیت پر مشتمل ہے خواہ مذہب امام کے خلاف ہو یا مذہب شافع کے کہ یہ کتاب مسلکی تعصب سے پاک ہے اس سے مقصود احقاق حق طلب صواب اور ابطال باطل ہے ۔ ان مصنفین مقلدین محض کی کتابوں کی طرح نہیں جو اپنے آباء سابقین کی تقلید میں جو سننے
His statement: 'And it does not deviate in deviation from reality' etc. The meaning is that the book 'Muslim' is based on mentioning issues formulated in the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Whichever school's view it is, it reports their exact statements without distortion or alteration, and does not mention contrary to reality. Or it means that according to human capability, as far as possible, statements based on truths are mentioned. This does not mean that what is truly correct with Allah is always mentioned, because that is exclusive to Allah—the Knower of the seen and unseen. Rather, by His grace, His vicegerents on earth—the prophets, messengers, and the perfect saints—may know it. This indicates that this book is based on truth, even if it goes against the Imam's school or Shafi'i's school, because the book is free from sectarian bias. Its aim is to establish truth, seek correctness, and refute falsehood. It is not like the books of mere blind followers who follow their ancestors in what they hear.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn phrase 'ولايميل ميلاما عن الواقعية' (and it does not deviate from reality). The commentator explains that the book 'Muslim' (the matn) objectively presents the positions of both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools without distortion. It faithfully reports each school's view. Alternatively, it means the book strives for truth to the extent of human capability, though it does not claim to know the absolute truth with Allah. The book is free from sectarian bias and aims to establish truth and refute falsehood. It contrasts with books of blind followers who simply imitate their ancestors.

Key Terms
واقعیہ (waqi'iyyah): Reality, factuality as distinguished from distortion.
مسلکی تعصب (maslaki ta'assub): Sectarian bias or partisanship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Bias

Key Takeaway
The book's methodology ensures that it presents the exact views of both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools without distortion, free from sectarian bias, aiming for truth and refutation of falsehood.

Author's Purpose: The Final Cause Behind Composing a Book
Defense of author's purpose and response to specification objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's stated purpose in writing 'Muslim al-Thubut' and explain his response to the objection about specifying only Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
A scholarly author's self-praise may serve an ‘illat ghā’iyya—a noble final cause—not arrogance.

In this front-matter passage, the commentator defends the author's introduction, explaining that his self-praise is not arrogance but a statement of purpose. He identifies possible final causes for writing the book, such as seeking truth, guiding students, or attaining divine reward. The passage also addresses an important objection: if the book covers other schools, why does it specify only Hanafis and Shafi'is? The answer reveals the book's focus on the primary polemical issues and an indirect censure of authors who ignore these two major schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the specific criticism raised by commentators: the author seems to boast, implying superiority over others.
The objection is about self-praise and the inconsistency of specifying only two schools.
2
Locate the author's response
Read where the author clarifies his purpose is to ensure that usul principles are not hidden, not to claim superiority.
Focus on the phrase 'lamrin ma aradtu' and the list of possible noble intentions.
3
Understand 'illat ghā'iyya'
Note the term's meaning: the final cause or ultimate purpose behind an action, here the motive for writing.
This is a key usul concept used to evaluate intentions behind rulings.
4
Analyze the specification objection
The critic wonders why the book mentions only Hanafi and Shafi'i schools when it also covers Mu'tazila and Shi'a.
This is a challenge to the author's consistency.
5
Follow the reply and its implications
The answer: most major disputes are between these two schools; others are incidental. Also, it indirectly censures authors who omit these schools.
The specification is justified by practical focus and serves a corrective purpose.

قوله ثم لامرما اردت أن احرر سفراً وافياً الخ، اس کا قول لامر میں تنوین تعظیم کی ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ ایک عظیم مقصد اس کتاب کی تصنیف کی علت غائیہ ہے امر عظیم مصنف کے نزدیک خواہ سلطان عصر کا تقرب ہو خواہ اپنے معاصر علماء پر اپنی علمی دھاگ اور ذہانت کا سکہ بٹھانا ہو چاہے اس فن کے طلبہ کو حق وصواب کی راہ دکھانا ہو یا سعادت دارین کا حصول مقصود ہو اور یہ علماء دین سے زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ سفر اگرہ کے ساتھ جمع اس کی اسفار آتی ہے دفتر ی عظیم و نیم کتاب کے معنی میں بولا جاتا ہے قرآن حکیم میں ہے کمثل الحمار تجمل اسفاراً۔ قـولـه - ولايميل ميلاما عن الواقعية الخ ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ کتاب «مسلم ، حنفی و شافعی مسلک میں وضع کردہ مسائل کے ذکر پر مبنی ہے جن کا جو مذہب ہے بعینہ من و عن ان کے اقوال کو بیان کیا گیا ہے کسی بھی مذہب کو توڑ مروڑ کر یا اس میں تغیر وتصرف بھیجا کر کے خلاف واقعہ نہیں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
یا یہ معنی ہے کہ طاقت بشریہ کے مطابق حتی الامکان حقائق پر مبنی اقوال ذکر کئے گئے ہیں۔ یہ معنی نہیں ہے کہ جو عند اللہ حق ہے دھی مذکور ہے اس لئے کہ یہ صرف اور صرف اللہ خالق قوم علیم وخبیر عالم الغیب والشھادۃ کی شان ہے ہاں اسکی عطاء سے اس کے خلفاء ارضین انبیاء مرسلین اور اولیاء کاملین جان سکتے ہیں۔
اس میں اشارہ ہے کہ یہ کتاب حقانیت پر مشتمل ہے خواہ مذہب امام کے خلاف ہو یا مذہب شافع کے کہ یہ کتاب مسلکی تعصب سے پاک ہے اس سے مقصود احقاق حق طلب صواب اور ابطال باطل ہے ۔ ان مصنفین مقلدین محض کی کتابوں کی طرح نہیں جو اپنے آباء سابقین کی تقلید میں جو سننے میں آیا خواہ صحیح خواہ غلط کتابوں کی زینت بنا دیا۔
اعتراض : ۔ مصنف کے حاشیہ سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ یہ کتاب ائمہ اربعہ کے مذہب پر بلکہ جملہ فرق باطلہ خصوصاً معتزلہ اور اہل تشیع کے اقوال کے ذکر پر بھی مشتمل ہے تو پھر بیان ذکر میں مذہب احناف وشوافع کی تخصیص کیوں کی ؟
جواب :۔ گو کہ اس کتاب میں احناف و شوافع کے علاوہ دوسرے مذاہب کا بھی ذکر ہے مگر اکثر خلافیات اصلا و مستقلا انہیں دونوں کے ہیں بقیہ فرق باطلہ کا ذکر ضمنا وتبعا قلیل الوجود ہے اس لئے خصوصیت کے ساتھ ان دونوں مذاہب کا ذکر کیا نیز مصنف کا اس سے ان مصنفین پر تعریض مقصود ہے جنکی کتابیں ان دونوں مذاہب عالیہ کے ذکر سے خالی ہیں۔
Authors with rational minds appear very forward in expressing their praise and boasting, but manifestation of knowledge and clarity does not necessitate that no one else is like them, or that the author has reached the level of the mujtahids who are called imams of this art. Rather, the author's purpose is only that some of the topics and principles laid down by the early and later scholars of usul should not remain hidden from them, and there is no arrogance or pride in this, as some commentators have criticized. Then his saying: 'lamrin ma aradtu an uharrira safran wafiyan' etc. His word 'lamrin' has a tanwin of glorification. Meaning: A great purpose is the final cause of composing this book. The great purpose in the author's view may be the proximity of the sultan of the age, or to impress his contemporaries with his scholarly reputation and intelligence, or to show the students of this art the path of truth and correctness, or to attain happiness in both worlds. And this is more apparent to the scholars of religion. Then his saying: 'la yamīlu maylāman an al-wāqi‘īya' etc. The meaning is that the book 'Muslim' is based on mentioning the issues laid down in the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools. Whatever the school of each, their statements are mentioned exactly, without twisting or altering any school, nor mentioning contrary to reality. Or it means that according to human ability, statements are mentioned as far as possible based on facts. It does not mean that what is true in the sight of Allah is mentioned, because that is solely the attribute of Allah, the Creator of all people, All-Knowing, All-Aware, Knower of the unseen and the witnessed. Yes, by His gift, His vicegerents on earth—the prophets, messengers, and the perfect awliya—can know it. This indicates that this book contains truth, even if it goes against the school of Abu Hanifa or the school of al-Shafi‘i; this book is free from sectarian bias. Its purpose is to establish truth, seek correctness, and refute falsehood. It is not like the books of those mere imitators who, in imitation of their predecessors, whatever they heard—whether correct or false—made it an ornament of the books. Objection: From the author's marginal note it appears that this book includes the schools of the four imams, and indeed also the statements of all false sects, especially the Mu‘tazila and the Shi‘a. Then why in the mention were the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools specified? Response: Although in this book, besides the Hanafis and Shafi‘is, other schools are also mentioned, most of the differences originally and independently belong to these two. The mention of the remaining false sects is incidental and subordinate, being very few. Therefore, these two schools are mentioned specifically. Also, the author intends to censure those authors whose books are devoid of mention of these two noble schools.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the preface of the author's own book. It begins by defending the author's self-praise, explaining that his purpose is not to claim superiority over others but to ensure that the topics and principles of usul al-fiqh are not hidden from the readers. The author then elaborates on his intention behind composing the book, listing possible noble motives such as seeking closeness to the ruler, displaying erudition, guiding students, or achieving eternal happiness. The phrase 'la yamilu maylaman an al-waqi‘iyya' is explained as meaning that the book faithfully presents the views of the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools without distortion. An objection is raised: if the book covers all schools including false sects like Mu‘tazila and Shi‘a, why does it specify only Hanafis and Shafi‘is? The answer is that the book primarily deals with these two because most of the polemical issues are between them, and mention of others is incidental. Also the author intends to criticize those who ignore these two major schools.

Key Terms
علت غائیہ (‘illat ghā’iyya): The final cause or purpose for an action; here, the author's motive for writing the book.
تعریض (ta‘rīḍ): Indirect censure or allusion; here, the author's implied criticism of other writers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the book 'Muslim al-Thubut' specify only the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools in its title despite also covering other sects?
A) Because the author is ignorant of other schools.
B) Because most of the polemical issues are between these two schools, and mention of others is incidental.
C) Because the author wants to exclude false sects.
D) Because the book was commissioned by the Hanafi and Shafi‘i rulers.

Key Takeaway
The author of 'Muslim al-Thubut' defends his preface by explaining that his self-praise has a noble final cause, and his specification of Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools is justified because most substantive disputes are between them, with other sects mentioned only incidentally.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Title and Structure of Muslim al-Thubut
Lexical and structural overview of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the metaphorical meaning of 'sihr' in the author's phrase and state the five-part structure of Muslim al-Thubut.

Core Idea
The book is so subtle it 'enchants' the reader; its structure is a preface, three articles, four principles, and a conclusion.

This passage from the commentary defines two key terms from the author's opening: 'sihr' and 'malakut'. It then presents the entire structure of Muslim al-Thubut, which is essential for navigating the work. Understanding this framework will help you grasp the overall plan of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key lexicon words
Locate the words 'sihr' and 'malakut' in the commentary and note their literal and metaphorical meanings.
2
Interpret 'sihr' metaphorically
Understand that 'sihr' here does not mean sorcery but refers to the subtlety and depth of the book that 'enchants' the reader.
The commentary cites al-Sihah dictionary: 'everything elegant and subtle is sihr'.
3
Memorize the five-part structure
Identify the five parts: Muqaddimah (preface), three Maqalat (articles), four Usul (principles), and Khatimah (conclusion).
The matn says: 'ala muqaddimah, thalath maqalat, arba‘ usul, khatimah.'
4
Understand the purpose of each part
The preface provides insight (basira), the articles cover fundamentals (mabadi), the principles address objectives (maqasid), and the conclusion discusses ijtihad and related topics.
Each part's function is given in the translation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله - سحرلا یدری - کروہ اور ہے جس کا ماخذ دقیق ہو صحاح میں ہے کل مالطف ما خذه ودق فھو سحر معنی یہ ہے کہ یہ کتاب ایسی مغلق اور دقیق ہے جس کی حقیقت حال معلوم نہیں ہوسکتی اس لئے کہ اسک مثل اور اسکی نظیر معدوم ہے اور شئی اپنے مثل سے پہچانی جاتی ہے یا یہ معنی ہے کہ یہ کتاب اپنے پڑھنے والوں کو مسحور کر دیتی ہے اس کا قول ملکوت اسم ہے ملک کے معنی میں، بادشاہی، تصرف پروردگاری، عزت و قدرت عالم قدس، ملائکہ کی دنیا و غیر ها معنی آتے ہیں صوفیوں کے نزدیک عالم ارواح کو کہتے ہیں، بعضوں نے بمعنی عالم غیب کے لکھا ہے۔ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ ملکوت اس فرشتہ کا نام ہے جو نعمتوں کے پہونچانے میں واسطہ ہے۔
متن المسلم : ألا الكتاب مرتب على مقدمة فيما يفيد البصيرة ومقالات في المبادى واصول فى المقاصد وخاتمة في الاجتهاد ونحوه
ترجمه: سنوا یہ کتاب ایک مقدمہ جو بصیرت کا فائدہ دے مقاصد کے شروع کرنے میں، تین مقالات پر مباری کے ذکر میں، چار اصول پر مقاصد کے بیان میں اور ایک خاتمہ پر اجتہاد غیرہ کے بیان کے لئے مرتب ہے۔
تشريح - قوله الكتاب - الکتاب پر الف لام عہد کا ہے مراد اس سے مصنف کا مؤلف یعنی مسلم الثبوت ہے جو ایک مقدمہ تین مقالات، چار اصول، اور ایک خاتمہ پر ترتیب دی گئی ہے مقدمہ
His saying: 'siḥr lā yudrā' - Ugliness? And it is that whose source is subtle. In the Sahah: 'Everything that is elegant in its acquisition and subtle is sihr.' Meaning: This book is so ambiguous and subtle that its reality cannot be known, because its like and its peer are non-existent, and a thing is recognized by its like. Or it means that this book enchants its readers. His saying: 'malakūt' is a noun meaning dominion, kingdom, divine disposition, honor and power, the holy world, the world of angels and others come in meaning. According to the Sufis, they call it the world of spirits. Some have written it meaning the unseen world. It has also been said that 'Malakut' is the name of the angel who is the intermediary in conveying blessings. The matn of al-Muslim: 'Indeed the book is arranged upon a preface that provides insight, and articles on the principles, and principles on the objectives, and a conclusion on ijtihad and the like.' Translation: Listen: This book is arranged with a preface that gives benefit of insight at the beginning of the objectives, three articles on the mention of the fundamentals, four principles on the expression of the objectives, and a conclusion for the expression of ijtihad and the like. Commentary - His saying: 'al-kitāb' - The definite article 'al' is for previous reference. What is meant by it is the author's composition, i.e., Muslim al-Thubut, which is arranged into one preface, three articles, four principles, and one conclusion. Preface...
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary by explaining two key words from the author's text. First, 'sihr' (magic) is interpreted not literally but as meaning something extremely subtle and refined, such that the book's depth cannot be fully grasped. The commentator cites the dictionary 'al-Sihah' to support this. Then 'malakut' (dominion) is defined in multiple senses: kingdom, the spiritual realm, the world of angels, or the unseen world. This leads to the matn, which is the actual text of 'Muslim al-Thubut' authored by the original writer. The matn states that the book is organized into five parts: a preface (to provide insight), three articles (dealing with foundational principles), four principles (regarding the main objectives), and a conclusion (on ijtihad and related topics). The commentary then begins explaining the first word 'al-kitāb', noting that 'al' refers to the specific book 'Muslim al-Thubut', and lists its parts, ending with 'preface' (to be continued).

Key Terms
سحر (siḥr): Here interpreted as 'subtlety' or 'refinement' that makes the book seem magical, not actual sorcery.
ملکوت (malakūt): Dominion, the spiritual realm, the world of angels or unseen.
مقدمہ (muqaddima): The prefatory section of the book that provides insight (basira).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many articles (maqalat) does Muslim al-Thubut contain?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Muslim al-Thubut is structured into a preface, three articles, four principles, and a conclusion, and its title's 'sihr' is a metaphor for profound subtlety.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Organization and Madhhab Scope of Musallam al-Thubut
Explains book's structure and madhhab scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the four-part structure of Musallam al-Thubut and explain why the commentary specifies only the Hanafi and Shafi'i madhhabs despite the book covering other views.

Core Idea
The book's introduction, essays on preliminaries, principles on objectives, and conclusion on ijtihad form a universal framework for usul textbooks.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, addresses two key features: the book's organizational structure and its madhhab coverage. The matn declares that the book is arranged upon an introduction, three essays, four principles, and a conclusion. The commentary then explains an objection: if the book mentions other madhhabs and even deviant sects, why does the description specify only Hanafi and Shafi'i? The answer reveals that the core disputes are between these two schools; other views are incidental. This lesson unpacks both the structure and the scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four parts from the matn
Locate in the source the statement that the book is arranged upon an introduction, three essays, four principles, and a conclusion. Note the Arabic terms.
The matn uses 'مقدمة', 'مقالات', 'اصول', 'خاتمة'.
2
Understand the inductive reason
The commentator explains that this division is based on inductive observation (istiqra') of how scholarly works are generally organized.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on practical observation.
3
Examine the objection about madhhab coverage
Read the objection: the book includes other madhhabs and deviant sects, so why specifically mention Hanafi and Shafi'i?
The objection is from the author's margin.
4
Analyze the answer
The answer: most disputes fundamentally involve these two schools; others are incidental (qalil al-wujud). The author also intends criticism of those who omit these two.
This shows the practical focus of the work.

Source Text
